[p.002] Front page Atria in brief Atria’s key indicators CEO’s review Strategy 2021–2025 Strategy 2016–2020 Operating environment Business area reviews Atria Finland Atria Sweden Atria Denmark & Estonia Atria Russia Research and Development Financial Statements and Corporate Governance Financial Statements and Corporate Governance Auditor’s report Corporate Governance Statement Investor reporting Contact information 2 Atria’s Annual Report 2020 Established in 1903, Atria is one of the leading meat and food companies in the Nordic countries, Russia and Estonia.
[p.002] Our company is highly appreciated by our customers, employees and owners.
[p.002] We have been producing food for more than 100 years, and we want to continue to do so, which is why our operations take account of the planet, people and product.
[p.002] Atria’s renewal and growth are based on commercial excellence and an efficient and responsible way of working.
[p.002] Our main product, good food, creates a better mood and sustainable value for all our stakeholders.
[p.002] In 2020, our net sales were approximately EUR 1.50 billion, and Atria had around 4,440 employees in Finland, Sweden, Denmark, Estonia and Russia.
[p.002] Atria Plc’s shares have been listed on the Nasdaq Helsinki since 1991.

[p.004] The calculation covers carbon dioxide emissions from Atria’s industrial production process in companies of which Atria owns more than 50%, in line with Scope 1 and Scope 2.
[p.004] Scope 1 (red) covers direct emissions from energy sources that are owned or controlled by the reporting company, and that are used for heating and production, for example.
[p.004] Scope 2 (purple) covers indirect emissions from purchased electricity, steam and heat production, and from cooling.
[p.004] Scope 2 reporting is based on a costbased calculation method and employs the emission values of known energy sources or the national residual mix.
[p.004] For Russia, the calculation employs the locationbased CO2 emission value reported by the International Energy Agency (IEA).

[p.005] Front page Atria in brief Atria’s key indicators CEO’s review Strategy 2021–2025 Strategy 2016–2020 Operating environment Business area reviews Atria Finland Atria Sweden Atria Denmark & Estonia Atria Russia Research and Development Financial Statements and Corporate Governance Financial Statements and Corporate Governance Auditor’s report Corporate Governance Statement Investor reporting Contact information Atria’s Annual Report 2020 Atria stayed on course despite the turbulent year Although 2020 was an exceptional year, Atria’s operations could be described as astoundingly solid.
[p.005] Our net sales increased, and all our business segments improved their results compared with the previous year.
[p.005] We also published our new strategy to become the winning northern European food company.
[p.005] 2020 was an exceptional year.
[p.005] The new year began with high expectations – everyone expected a normal continuation of 2019.
[p.005] At the turn of the year, we had all seen and heard on the news that a new viral respiratory infection had been discovered in Wuhan in China.
[p.005] From a European perspective, it felt far away at the time, but by February, the same virus was already putting Europe on the rack as well.
[p.005] From then on, 2020 became a year of living with Covid-19.
[p.005] Atria did well in navigating the exceptional year.
[p.005] The company’s net sales increased by EUR 52.7 million to a total of EUR 1,504.0 million.
[p.005] Our EBIT increased to EUR 40.5 million from approximately EUR 31 million, which is 30 % increase from 2019.
[p.005] All our business segments improved their results compared with the previous year.
[p.005] Free cash flow increased from the previous year by more than EUR 7 million and was EUR 59.0 million in 2020.
[p.005] *** The food industry is characterised by steady overall demand even in exceptional circumstances.
[p.005] Variation only occurs in where people buy their food and the food they buy.
[p.005] Due to the restrictions implemented to stop the spread of the coronavirus, and the voluntary measures taken by various parties, people did not move about as much.
[p.005] Restrictions were placed on hobbies, and some people started working remotely.
[p.005] At times, the restaurant business was shut down completely.
[p.005] As people spent more time at home, they purchased their food from retailers.
[p.005] In turn, fewer people were eating out.
[p.005] Atria’s sales to retailers increased by 10 per cent, while sales to Food Service customers decreased by 20%.
[p.005] In the summer, our sales development took a fascinating turn: as the number of corona cases decreased, and things returned to normal for a while, sales to Food Service customers quickly recovered to their previous level.
[p.005] There seems to be a strong tendency to return to our previous way of life as soon as the situation allows it.
[p.005] *** Poultry consumption continues to increase.
[p.005] This is a global phenomenon.
[p.005] Pork consumption in Finland has been decreasing for a few years, and the same downward trend continued in 2020.
[p.005] Beef consumption has remained unchanged.
[p.005] One interesting development is the growth of the sausage market – the coronavirus has brought us back to basics, to classics such as sausages.
[p.005] These basics include chicken and minced meat.
[p.005] It was a rocky year for convenience foods, as people prepared more meals at home than usual.
[p.005] Large fluctuations in demand from one week or month “The food industry is characterised by steady overall demand even in exceptional circumstances.” CEO’S REVIEW 6

[p.006] So we are already used to fluctuating demand, and this has made it easier for us to adapt to the corona time.
[p.006] We have put all our energy into focusing on the basics.
[p.006] On the other hand, we have not delayed forward-looking measures.
[p.006] Instead, we have strived to maintain business as usual wherever possible.
[p.006] For example, investments have not been postponed.
[p.006] *** In late 2020, we published our new strategy to become the winning northern European food company.
[p.006] “Winning” here refers to operational leadership: Atria wants to be a company that leads by example, reforming the entire industry.
[p.006] Our industrial operations are located in northern Europe.
[p.006] We are a food company with a versatile product offering that includes delicious solutions for all kinds of meals.
[p.006] The new strategy is a continuation of our Healthy Growth Strategy, which offers a solid foundation for building something new.
[p.006] In recent years, we have enhanced our productivity through means like improved tools for operational monitoring and control.
[p.006] We are now aiming to improve our cost-effectiveness through a straightforward approach.
[p.006] We already have an excellent handle on market intelligence.
[p.006] It is time to make more use of this data.
[p.006] We want to be a first-class partner for our customers.
[p.006] During the pandemic, many of us at Atria have learned a lot of things the hard way.
[p.006] More than ever, we have come to understand the value of long-term partnerships and the difficulty of building new networks.
[p.006] I want to thank all our customers for placing your trust in Atria.
[p.006] 2020 was a tough year for our personnel.
[p.006] We have had to work in exceptional circumstances, in a situation where nobody knows how long the unusual arrangements will last.
[p.006] However, everyone has done a great job, and both individual employees and different parts of the organisation have clearly demonstrated their willingness to take responsibility.
[p.006] This willpower and the performance it has driven have kept the situation under control.
[p.006] Thank you all.
[p.006] I also want to thank our business partners and shareholders, who have helped us to succeed and thrive in 2020.
[p.006] Seinäjoki, March 2021 Juha Gröhn CEO “Our EBIT increased to EUR 40.5 million from approximately EUR 31 million in 2019.
[p.006] All our business segments improved their results.” CEO’S REVIEW 7

[p.009] Front page Atria in brief Atria’s key indicators CEO’s review Strategy 2021–2025 Strategy 2016–2020 Operating environment Business area reviews Atria Finland Atria Sweden Atria Denmark & Estonia Atria Russia Research and Development Financial Statements and Corporate Governance Financial Statements and Corporate Governance Auditor’s report Corporate Governance Statement Investor reporting Contact information Atria’s Annual Report 2020 Our strategic priorities We have confirmed six strategic priorities for the 2021–2025 strategy period.
[p.009] Win big in poultry Poultry consumption is increasing steadily in Finland and globally.
[p.009] We are aiming for market leadership in poultry in Finland and are also seeking to strengthen our position in Sweden.
[p.009] The importance of this goal is reflected in our decision to invest in a new poultry unit.
[p.009] We want to provide our customers and consumers with interesting channel options in all product segments.
[p.009] Expand in convenience foods Convenience foods are a growing market, because people are increasingly consuming ready-made food.
[p.009] By using customer and market information, we can provide our customers with the products they want and introduce interesting new products in our selections.
[p.009] Our strengths are high quality in all price ranges and strong brands.
[p.009] Sustainable, reliable and traceable production are our key competitive advantages.
[p.009] Strengthen in Food Service, including fast food The Food Service market continues to grow, because people are increasingly eating out.
[p.009] We are aiming to grow faster than the market.
[p.009] We seek to achieve this by strengthening ATRIA PLC | STRATEGY 2021–2025 customer relationships in the Food Service and fast food sectors in all our business areas.
[p.009] In the fast food sector, our growth recipe is to increase the number of sales points and develop new products.
[p.009] Our strengths are a solid supply chain, reliability, and a high level of product safety and service.
[p.009] Grow profitably in Sweden In Sweden, our goal is to improve the profitability of our operations and achieve growth.
[p.009] We are seeking growth by increasing our share in retail, and in the Food Service and fast food markets.
[p.009] We improve profitability through increased operational efficiency.
[p.009] Optimize red meat Our goal is to improve the profitability of red meat.
[p.009] We seek to achieve this by improving operational efficiency, product category management and selection development.
[p.009] Strengthening export customer relationships also plays a key role in improving profitability.
[p.009] Drive next level supply chain efficiency Our goal is to improve supply chain efficiency in every operation, from order to delivery.
[p.009] This is our goal in all business areas.
[p.009] We are improving efficiency by investing in the latest technology, using monitoring data and strengthening our employees’ competence.

[p.010] The strategy responds to changes in consumer purchasing behaviour in particular.
[p.010] Awareness of sustainable food choices and increased demand for convenience foods, and especially poultry, are highlighted in purchasing decisions.
[p.010] The Food Service channel and the popularity of private labels are also increasing.
[p.010] The uncertainty of the international meat and food market and poor predictability pose a key challenge to the entire sector.
[p.010] Atria’s new strategy responds to the following changes that will have a material impact on the food sector between 2021 and 2025: Proteins In terms of demand, the focus continues to shift from red meat to poultry and plant-based options.
[p.010] Categories Demand for convenience foods, ready-made foods and snacking is growing.
[p.010] Consumers Consumers’ awareness of healthy lifestyles, sustainable development and animal welfare is increasing.
[p.010] Macroeconomy Economic instability and uncertainty, as well as protectionism and local focus, are increasing.
[p.010] Channels • Demand and new opportunities in the Food Service sector are growing.
[p.010] • The importance of digital channels continues to grow, and the growth of private labels continues.

[p.010] During the previous period, Atria implemented significant efficiency programmes and investments to improve its operational productivity and competitiveness.
[p.010] At the same time, the company succeeded in strengthening its equity ratio.

[p.011] Front page Atria in brief Atria’s key indicators CEO’s review Strategy 2021–2025 Strategy 2016–2020 Operating environment Business area reviews Atria Finland Atria Sweden Atria Denmark & Estonia Atria Russia Research and Development Financial Statements and Corporate Governance Financial Statements and Corporate Governance Auditor’s report Corporate Governance Statement Investor reporting Contact information Atria’s Annual Report 2020 ATRIA PLC | STRATEGY 2016–2020 Atria’s Healthy Growth strategy highlighted profitability Atria’s Healthy Growth strategy period ended at the close of 2020.
[p.011] The focus of the strategy period was on profitability.
[p.011] Other key goals included improving profitability, accelerating growth and increasing shareholder value systematically over the long term.
[p.011] During the 2016–2020 strategy period, Atria aimed to grow in a mainly organic manner by developing and expanding its existing operations.
[p.011] The company sought to drive growth by developing new product segments and expanding into new market areas.
[p.011] In this respect, the most significant achievement was entry into the Chinese pork market.
[p.011] Alongside organic growth, Atria actively identified opportunities for acquisitions and other arrangements generating healthy growth.
[p.011] These supplemented existing business operations, as well as offering opportunities to create entirely new product segments or enter new market areas.
[p.011] The most significant acquisitions in Finland were the Kaivon Liha Kaunismaa beef and the Domretor convenience food companies.
[p.011] In Sweden, Atria acquired the Lagerbergs poultry company.
[p.011] Atria managed its Healthy Growth strategy through three main themes: commercial excellence; efficient operations; and the Atria Way of Work.
[p.011] More information about the most important theme-specific successes of the strategy period is provided in the Board of Directors’ report (Financial Review, p.
[p.011] 46).

[p.011] This investment of around EUR 36 million has enabled Atria to improve the productivity of the pig-cutting plant and the competitiveness of its entire pork chain for the domestic and export markets.
[p.011] Lagerbergs poultry company: EUR 33 million Atria entered the growing Swedish fresh poultry market by acquiring Lagerbergs in 2016.
[p.011] The acquisition of around EUR 19 million was supplemented by an investment programme of around EUR 14 million, through which Atria has strongly improved the productivity and competitiveness of the entire production chain.

[p.012] • In Russia, 200 new Sibylla outlets were opened.

[p.012] • Atria’s Way of Leading programmes continued to ensure a successful future management culture for the various business areas.
[p.012] • The Safely Home from Atria occupational safety and health programme achieved the best result in Atria’s history.

[p.013] Front page Atria in brief Atria’s key indicators CEO’s review Strategy 2021–2025 Strategy 2016–2020 Operating environment Business area reviews Atria Finland Atria Sweden Atria Denmark & Estonia Atria Russia Research and Development Financial Statements and Corporate Governance Financial Statements and Corporate Governance Auditor’s report Corporate Governance Statement Investor reporting Contact information Atria’s Annual Report 2020 ATRIA PLC | OPERATING ENVIRONMENT Some Covid-19 practices likely to become permanent Atria Finland’s Senior Occupational Health Physician Timo Kinnunen believes that some of the practices implemented by Atria during the Covid-19 pandemic are likely to become permanent: “Respiratory protection will be used more often than before, and the importance of good hand hygiene will be highlighted.
[p.013] Remote meetings will become more common, reducing the need for business trips.
[p.013] The coronavirus also serves as a stern warning that will make us treat infectious diseases in general with more respect and caution going forward.” Atria handled the Covid-19 pandemic well The year 2020 was strongly marked by the Covid-19 pandemic.
[p.013] The highly contagious coronavirus disease spread far and wide across the world, impacting the lives of individual people, and companies and entire countries.
[p.013] When the infectious disease reached Europe, and Atria’s countries of operations in particular, we immediately set the main company-wide goals for preventing its spread.
[p.013] Atria’s goals for preventing the spread of the SARS-CoV-2 virus remained the same throughout the period under review: preventing the spread of the virus; protecting our personnel; and safeguarding Atria’s operations throughout the chain.
[p.013] The exceptional situations and changes in the operating environment also required management to step up to the plate.
[p.013] The management teams of the Group and the individual business areas were involved in outlining Atria’s approach.
[p.013] The Covid-19 task forces established by the Group and all business areas were responsible for maintaining a continuous view of the situation, drafting new guidelines and planning new practices.
[p.013] Atria followed the instructions and guidelines issued by the authorities in all its operations.
[p.013] The SARS-CoV-2 virus is mainly transmitted through droplets, but also through aerosols at close range.
[p.013] There have been no confirmed cases of contact transmission through packaging, food products or goods.
[p.013] The most important new practices implemented by Atria were based on preventing the spread of the coronavirus with respiratory protection, good hand hygiene and social distancing.
[p.013] Many people at Atria started working remotely early in the spring of 2020, and this will continue in the spring of 2021.
[p.013] Atria issued guidelines on travel, including travel bans, and limited gatherings and visits to our locations.
[p.013] Atria has solid safety systems in place even in normal times.
[p.013] We are used to working in the sphere of foodrelated microbes, and are familiar with risk management and product safety practices.
[p.013] The same risk minimisation tools and product safety management practices are also well-suited to tackling the coronavirus.
[p.013] In addition, we have had to take into account that this is a human infectious disease, a human pandemic.
[p.013] Atria handled the exceptional circumstances of the pandemic well.
[p.013] Apart from the new practices, the epidemic did not greatly affect our operations, and Atria was able to meet consumer demand and customer requirements.
[p.013] Merja Leino EVP, Sustainability Atria Plc 14

[p.014] The increase in retailer sales was approximately 10 per cent.
[p.014] Sales to Food Service and Fast Food customers decreased by approximately 20 per cent due to the coronavirus restrictions implemented in various business areas.

[p.017] Consumers are increasingly interested in high-quality, ecological, customised and safe food products.
[p.017] The consumption of animal-based products continues to grow, but the demand for processed plant-based products is also increasing.
[p.017] The demand and supply of pork are slowly finding a balance.

[p.017] In 2021 production is forecast to increase about 10%.
[p.017] Chinese pork imports China’s share of global pork imports has risen to about 40%.
[p.017] In 2020, the reduced domestic supply of pork together with high prices pushed China’s total meat imports to a record level of nearly 10 million tonnes.

[p.018] Front page Atria in brief Atria’s key indicators CEO’s review Strategy 2021–2025 Strategy 2016–2020 Operating environment Business area reviews Atria Finland Atria Sweden Atria Denmark & Estonia Atria Russia Research and Development Financial Statements and Corporate Governance Financial Statements and Corporate Governance Auditor’s report Corporate Governance Statement Investor reporting Contact information Atria’s Annual Report 2020 Strong growth for Atria’s pork exports Atria’s export of pork to China increased to over 20 million kilos in 2020.
[p.018] This accounts for almost 30% of the volume of meat processed by Atria.
[p.018] Exports to other key export countries, such as South Korea and Sweden, also increased.
[p.018] In addition, Atria signed a new cooperation agreement with a Japanese restaurant chain.
[p.018] In total, Atria’s exports increased by about 50% from 2019.
[p.018] It is important to Atria’s export customers that the products are clean, safe and traceable, and that the rearing of the animals is antibiotic-free.
[p.018] Antibiotic-free pork for a Japanese restaurant chain Atria signed a cooperation agreement with a Japanese restaurant chain for the export of Finnish antibiotic-free pork to Japan.
[p.018] The Japanese Bikkuri Donkey family restaurant chain uses Atria pork in its burger steaks.
[p.018] Bikkuri Donkey is part of the Aleph Inc. Group, which is committed to sustainable development.
[p.018] Its restaurants only use responsibly produced ingredients.

[p.019] Front page Atria in brief Atria’s key indicators CEO’s review Strategy 2021–2025 Strategy 2016–2020 Operating environment Business area reviews Atria Finland Atria Sweden Atria Denmark & Estonia Atria Russia Research and Development Financial Statements and Corporate Governance Financial Statements and Corporate Governance Auditor’s report Corporate Governance Statement Investor reporting Contact information Atria’s Annual Report 2020 ATRIA PLC | OPERATING ENVIRONMENT | FINNISH POULTRY MARKET Poultry market growth in Finland in 2000–2020 Poultry consumption has increased steadily in Finland throughout the 2000s.
[p.019] In 2020, both poultry consumption and production increased by about 4%.
[p.019] The domestic share of consumption also increased.
[p.019] Forecast for poultry consumption in Finland According to consumption forecasts by Atria, poultry consumption (mainly chicken products) in Finland will exceed 200 million kilos by 2030 if the consumption trend remains similar to that between 2011 and 2020, when the average annual growth rate was 3.8%.
[p.019] 160 140 120 100 80 60 40 20 0 Production Consumption Import Source: Kantar TNS 2021 Million kg of bone-in meat Million kg 2010 2012 2014 2016 2018 2020 2022f 2024f 2026f 2028f 2030f 250 200 150 100 50 0 Consumption forecast scenarios: +4% +3% +2% Source: Atria Insight, 2019 Atria introduced carbon footprint markings on chicken product packaging The first carbon footprint-marked chicken products were sold in retail stores in December 2020.
[p.019] As far as we know, Atria is the first producer to use carbon footprint labelling on its chicken products.
[p.019] Farm-specific traceability of the meat raw material enables product-specific carbon footprint labelling.
[p.019] The Alatalo farm’s chicken products were the first to carry a carbon footprint label.
[p.019] As farm-specific calculations are completed for more farms, more and more products will get a carbon footprint marking.
[p.019] The label shows the climate impact of the product’s entire production chain in terms of carbon dioxide.
[p.019] The calculation also takes into account industrial production and packaging.
[p.019] The carbon footprint calculation was carried out in cooperation with Envitecpolis Oy and Atria producers.

[p.020] Front page Atria in brief Atria’s key indicators CEO’s review Strategy 2021–2025 Strategy 2016–2020 Operating environment Business area reviews Atria Finland Atria Sweden Atria Denmark & Estonia Atria Russia Research and Development Financial Statements and Corporate Governance Financial Statements and Corporate Governance Auditor’s report Corporate Governance Statement Investor reporting Contact information Atria’s Annual Report 2020 The decision to build a new poultry plant was confirmed In October, Atria confirmed the decision to build a new poultry plant in Nurmo.
[p.020] The investment is the largest in Atria’s history and extremely important to the company.
[p.020] The value of the investment is approximately EUR 155 million, and it will increase Atria Finland’s poultry production capacity by approximately 40%.
[p.020] The construction of the new poultry plant meets the increased demand for chicken and strengthens Atria’s position as the market leader in chicken products.
[p.020] The consumption of chicken has grown strongly both in Finland and globally for many years, and it is expected to keep growing.
[p.020] The new plant will be completed in 2024.
[p.020] Further information about the progress of the investment is available on our website at www.atria.fi/konserni/ ajankohtaista/atrian-siipikarjainvestointi-2024/.

[p.022] Front page Atria in brief Atria’s key indicators CEO’s review Strategy 2021–2025 Strategy 2016–2020 Operating environment Business area reviews Atria Finland Atria Sweden Atria Denmark & Estonia Atria Russia Research and Development Financial Statements and Corporate Governance Financial Statements and Corporate Governance Auditor’s report Corporate Governance Statement Investor reporting Contact information Atria’s Annual Report 2020 Atria Finland Atria Finland is responsible for Atria’s operations in Finland.
[p.022] Atria Finland develops, produces, markets and sells fresh meat and other food products, in addition to providing related services.
[p.022] Atria is the market leader in the slaughterhouse industry and many of its product categories in Finland.
[p.022] It also has substantial export operations.
[p.022] In 2020, Atria Finland’s net sales were EUR 1,066.3 million, and the company had about 2,400 employees.
[p.022] All of the meat used in Atria brand is Finnish.

[p.023] Front page Atria in brief Atria’s key indicators CEO’s review Strategy 2021–2025 Strategy 2016–2020 Operating environment Business area reviews Atria Finland Atria Sweden Atria Denmark & Estonia Atria Russia Research and Development Financial Statements and Corporate Governance Financial Statements and Corporate Governance Auditor’s report Corporate Governance Statement Investor reporting Contact information Atria’s Annual Report 2020 Net sales (EUR million) The net sales of Atria Finland grew by EUR 32.5 million compared to the previous year, and amounted to EUR 1,066.3 million.
[p.023] Net sales were boosted by increased sales to the retail sector and export customers.
[p.023] Pork exports to China increased significantly and the sales of Atria’s product categories in the Finnish retail trade also grew more strongly than in the previous year.
[p.023] Sales to Food Service customers decreased significantly due to the coronavirus pandemic.
[p.023] EBIT (EUR million) Atria Finland’s EBIT increased EUR 3.1 million from the previous year to EUR 43.1 million.
[p.023] This was 4.0% of net sales.
[p.023] Profitability improved mostly because of increased net sales, improved productivity and effective cost control.
[p.023] Strong growth under challenging circumstances The year 2020 was good for Atria Finland’s growth and profitability.
[p.023] Despite the coronavirus pandemic making our operating environment exceptionally challenging and uncertain, we succeeded to make stronger progress than in the previous year in two of our main channels, retail trade and exports.
[p.023] In our third main channel, the Food Service sector, the measures taken to limit the coronavirus pandemic reduced the industry’s total earnings by about one-fifth.
[p.023] Atria’s development was similar to the general development of the industry.
[p.023] The coronavirus pandemic also changed the Finnish consumer demand for food dramatically.
[p.023] Demand for food grew at the same rate as cooking at home, and good home-cooked meals became highly valued.
[p.023] This was directly reflected in Atria’s sales to the retail sector.
[p.023] The market for Atria’s cooking, poultry and consumer-packed meat product categories grew by almost 10%.
[p.023] Atria’s supplier share grew in all product categories, as did the sales of Atria’s own brands.
[p.023] Overall development was strong.
[p.023] The same is true of Atria’s pork exports to China: they more than doubled from the previous year to over 20 million kilos.
[p.023] This was almost 30% of the pork produced by the Nurmo plant.
[p.023] The consumption of meat in Finland remained stable.
[p.023] Ninety-three per cent of Finns eat meat – and specifically meat produced in Finland.
[p.023] About 83% of all meat consumed in Finland was domestically produced.
[p.023] These figures are very important for Atria’s future growth.
[p.023] After all, the year 2020 saw the largest investment decision in our history, amounting to approximately EUR 155 million, to build a new poultry unit near the Nurmo plants.

[p.029] -5 -6 -7 -8 MEUR X,X 3 2 1 0 -1 -2 -3 -4 -5 EBIT % -2.0 -6.1 On the road to profitable growth For the second year running, Atria Sweden made progress in achieving its key strategic goal, the improvement of profitability.
[p.029] We improved our result by EUR 4.1 million.
[p.029] The operating loss decreased to one third compared to the corresponding period of the previous year.
[p.029] A central reason for our improved performance was the improving competitiveness and profitability of our poultry business.
[p.029] The significant improvement in profitability was a good outcome in the Swedish food market hit by the pandemic.
[p.029] The measures to restrict the spreading of the coronavirus significantly weakened Atria’s Food Service and Fast Food sales, but the effects on retail sales were the opposite.
[p.029] The sales of Atria’s products to the retail trade grew exceptionally strongly, both in terms of volume and value.
[p.029] The value of the poultry product market grew the most, by as much as 19.2%.
[p.029] The market for sausages also grew by 15.7%.
[p.029] These markets are very important to Atria, and we were able to increase our supplier share in both.
[p.029] Although the Swedish Food Service market shrank by about 20% last year, Atria’s development was not equally poor.
[p.029] We were able to slightly strengthen our market position.
[p.029] We benefited from our large customer base that includes both private and public professional kitchens.
[p.029] We actively collaborated with both of these customer groups in product development and sales.
[p.029] We were able to adapt our supply to the changes in demand and flexibly launched new products on the market, especially chicken products.
[p.029] The sales of Finnish beef and pork to professional kitchens also developed favourably.

[p.038] Growth in retail sales Atria Russia has three sales channels for its product categories: the retail sector, Sibylla customers and Food Service customers.
[p.038] Of these three, only the retail sector remained open almost as usual throughout the pandemic year.
[p.038] Atria’s sales to the retail trade developed well both in terms of sales volume and value in local currency.
[p.038] The growth was driven above all by the premium Casademont brand.
[p.038] The sales of its product categories increased throughout the year.
[p.038] In contrast, the sales of the low-price Pit-Product brand fell.
[p.038] Price competition in the Pit product categories was fierce.
[p.038] Our cooperation with the leading Russian retail chains X5, Lenta and Okey became more diverse and Atria was also able to expand its offering geographically.
[p.038] The development of the Sibylla concept was varied.
[p.038] Orders fell sharply when the pandemic started in the spring, but started to recover in the summer and eventually increased from the previous year.
[p.038] The number of Sibylla sales outlets in Russia increased by about 200 to a total of about 4,300.
[p.038] Orders and deliveries through Atria’s third channel, Food Service customers, fell considerably.
[p.038] The operating conditions for the whole industry deteriorated dramatically: the number of bankruptcies was high and restaurant sales fell by about 40% from the previous year.
[p.038] Although Atria’s production and commercial operations developed favourably in the demanding circumstances, the profitability of the operations remained poor.
[p.038] The weak performance was partly due to higher raw material prices.
[p.038] Depending on the type of meat, prices rose by 10–15%.

[p.039] Daily operational efficiency • Organisational streamlining continued for the purpose of achieving strategic goals.
[p.039] Resource optimisation • Resource efficiency was improved by harmonising the material efficiency of packaging and by optimising raw materials and fine-tuning logistics.
[p.039] Atria Way of Leading • The continuation of Atria’s Way of Leading and Atria’s Way to Work trainings was reflected positively in the job satisfaction experienced by employees.

[p.045] Front page Atria in brief Atria’s key indicators CEO’s review Strategy 2021–2025 Strategy 2016–2020 Operating environment Business area reviews Atria Finland Atria Sweden Atria Denmark & Estonia Atria Russia Research and Development Financial Statements and Corporate Governance Financial Statements and Corporate Governance Auditor’s report Corporate Governance Statement Investor reporting Contact information Atria’s Annual Report 2020 REPORT BY THE BOARD OF DIRECTORS 1 JANUARY–31 DECEMBER 2020 Atria’s management of challenges during exceptional circumstances good – in terms of growth and results, 2020 was a strong year for Atria The year 2020 will be marked in Atria’s history as an exceptional one.
[p.045] As of March, the operating environment changed into something entirely different than anticipated due to the COVID-19 pandemic.
[p.045] Atria’s organisation and people demonstrated an excellent ability to adjust to changes and a desire to stick to the set goals and targets.
[p.045] From the very start of the pandemic, Atria set itself two goals: continuing deliveries to customers without disruption and ensuring that its personnel stays healthy.
[p.045] In terms of these goals, 2020 was a successful year.
[p.045] In terms of growth and the result, Atria’s year was strong.
[p.045] The implementation of the strategy proceeded successfully.
[p.045] Atria Group’s net sales increased by nearly EUR 53 million year-on-year.
[p.045] EBIT improved by around EUR 9 million.
[p.045] One corporate acquisition was carried out in 2020: Atria acquired the entire share capital of Domretor Oy, a contract manufacturer in the food industry.
[p.045] Domretor Oy has been an associated company of Atria since 2013, when Atria acquired a 24.9% of Domretor’s shares.
[p.045] Atria’s balance sheet and financial position were good during the review period.
[p.045] Free cash flow was EUR 59.0 million (EUR 51.0 million).
[p.045] THE HEALTHY GROWTH STRATEGY PERIOD 2016–2020 Atria’s Healthy Growth strategy period concluded at the end of 2020.
[p.045] Its key objectives were to improve profitability, accelerate growth and increase shareholder value systematically over the long term.
[p.045] Atria’s goal was to grow mainly organically, by developing and expanding its existing business operations.
[p.045] The company sought to drive growth by developing new product segments and expanding into new market areas.
[p.045] Alongside organic growth, Atria actively identified opportunities for acquisitions and other arrangements generating healthy growth.
[p.045] The Healthy Growth strategy was led through three main themes: 1.
[p.045] Commercial excellence 2.
[p.045] Efficiency 3.
[p.045] Atria’s Way of Work The most important successes by theme during the 2016–2020 strategy period were as follows: 1.
[p.045] Commercial excellence • Product and packaging innovations, including entirely new type of packaging for minced meat.
[p.045] • The first pork exports to China and the increase of exporting.
[p.045] 2.
[p.045] Efficiency • The commissioning of the new pig-cutting plant representing world-class technology in 2017.
[p.045] The new investment has improved the pig-cutting plant’s productivity and the entire pork production chain’s competitiveness.
[p.045] • Significant investments in the development of Atria Sweden’s poultry business.
[p.045] • Investments in the development of the company’s own feed production.
[p.045] • Initiation of the planning and implementation of Atria Finland’s new poultry plant investment.
[p.045] 3.
[p.045] Atria’s Way of Work • Placing responsibility at the core of the business strategy and initiating the Responsible Atria programme with the aim of achieving a carbon-neutral food chain by 2035.
[p.045] • Building Finland’s biggest solar power park next to Atria’s Nurmo plant.
[p.045] • The launch of the Safely Home from Atria occupational safety and health programme and a significant reduction in the number of occupational accidents.
[p.045] 4.
[p.045] Conclusion of corporate acquisitions • The acquisition of Lagerberg i Norjeby AB, Well-Beef Ltd. and Domretor Oy.
[p.045] The strategy revision project was launched in late 2019, and the new strategy was published in the autumn of 2020.

[p.046] Front page Atria in brief Atria’s key indicators CEO’s review Strategy 2021–2025 Strategy 2016–2020 Operating environment Business area reviews Atria Finland Atria Sweden Atria Denmark & Estonia Atria Russia Research and Development Financial Statements and Corporate Governance Financial Statements and Corporate Governance Auditor’s report Corporate Governance Statement Investor reporting Contact information Atria’s Annual Report 2020 New strategy: The Winning Northern European Food Company The new strategy was completed in the autumn of 2020 and its communication was launched in October 2020.
[p.046] The principal objective of the revised strategy is for Atria to be the winning food company in northern Europe with: • strong financial performance; • the most desired brands; • preferred partner for the customers; • committed people; • leader in sustainability; and • best partner for owner-producers.
[p.046] The most important changes in the operating environment which influenced the new strategy related to consumers’ purchasing behaviour.
[p.046] Awareness of sustainable food choices and increased demand for convenience foods, especially poultry, are accentuated in purchasing decisions.
[p.046] The popularity of the food service channel and private labels is also increasing.
[p.046] The uncertainty in the markets over the past year has had an impact of the food industry’s outlook.

[p.047] Front page Atria in brief Atria’s key indicators CEO’s review Strategy 2021–2025 Strategy 2016–2020 Operating environment Business area reviews Atria Finland Atria Sweden Atria Denmark & Estonia Atria Russia Research and Development Financial Statements and Corporate Governance Financial Statements and Corporate Governance Auditor’s report Corporate Governance Statement Investor reporting Contact information Atria’s Annual Report 2020 REPORT BY THE BOARD OF DIRECTORS 1 JANUARY–31 DECEMBER 2020 It is essential for the achievement of the objectives to continue investments aiming to improve commercial excellence, efficiency and Atria’s Way of Work.
[p.047] In addition, it is particularly important for us to be successful in the six focal points most important in terms of our strategy’s performance.
[p.047] These focal points are: • win pig in poultry • expand in convenience foods • strengthen in Food Service, including fast food • grow profitably in Sweden • optimize red meat • drive next level in supply chain efficiency.
[p.047] Atria’s financial targets in 2021–2025 are as follows: • EBIT .............................................................5% • Equity ratio: .............................................
[p.047] 40% • Return on equity: ....................................10% • Capital distribution: ................................50% of the profit for the period • Growth above market Financial review 2020 Atria Group’s full-year net sales amounted to EUR 1504.0 million (EUR 1451.3 million).
[p.047] EBIT was EUR 40.5 million (EUR 31.1 million).
[p.047] Atria Group’s net sales increased due to good retail sector sales and exports.
[p.047] Sales to Food Service customers declined by roughly 20% compared to the previous year.
[p.047] The Group’s EBIT improved as a result of the growth in net sales, the good development of exports and lower costs..
[p.047] The exceptional circumstances brought about by the coronavirus pandemic impacted Atria’s operating environment as of the end of the first quarter.
[p.047] The national restrictions and recommendations related to restaurant activities and public food services had an impact on Atria’s business.
[p.047] The opening hours and customer numbers of restaurants have been restricted, and the reduced travel and mobility of people has also decreased food sales in fast food restaurants and service stations.
[p.047] The popularity of everyday meals sold to retail stores grew suddenly as people began preparing for the exceptional situation in late March.
[p.047] Sales volumes to fast food and Food Service customers declined considerably in April–May.
[p.047] Food Service sales began to increase alongside the gradual easing of the coronavirus restrictions and the market began to recover towards the end of the second quarter.
[p.047] Even so, it did not rebound to the level preceding the pandemic by the end of September.
[p.047] During the last quarter of the year, the restrictions were again tightened, which reduced sales to Food Service customers.
[p.047] Sales to the retail sector have been significantly higher than in the year before.
[p.047] The shift to exceptional circumstances in Atria’s operations was carried out rapidly so that the company was able to remain operational.
[p.047] The uninterrupted continuance of operations and ensuring the delivery reliability of products were Atria’s primary tasks, in addition to ensuring the personnel’s health and working capacity.
[p.047] The production plants adopted new practices aiming to prevent the spread of a possible viral infection.
[p.047] The special arrangements are still in use and have incurred extra costs.
[p.047] On the other hand, the shift to remote working and the end of business travel have accumulated savings.
[p.047] Atria has been successful in its objective of ensuring the personnel’s health and working capacity and maintaining the delivery reliability of products.
[p.047] Atria Finland’s full-year net sales were EUR 1,066.3 million (EUR 1,033.8 million).
[p.047] The increase in net sales was attributable to increased sales to the retail sector and export customers.
[p.047] The sales of Food Service products declined by 20% compared to the year before due to coronavirus restrictions.
[p.047] The company’s EBIT increased to EUR 43.1 million (EUR 40.0 million).
[p.047] The increase in EBIT was attributable to increased net sales, the good development of exports and improved productivity.
[p.047] The coronavirus pandemic has resulted in extra costs, but their negative impact on the result was mitigated by a reduction in the statutory pension insurance contribution.
[p.047] In October, Atria confirmed the decision to build a new poultry plant in Nurmo.
[p.047] The investment is the largest in Atria’s history and extremely important to the company.
[p.047] The value of the investment is approximately EUR 155 million, and it will increase Atria Finland’s poultry production capacity by approximately 40%.

[p.048] Front page Atria in brief Atria’s key indicators CEO’s review Strategy 2021–2025 Strategy 2016–2020 Operating environment Business area reviews Atria Finland Atria Sweden Atria Denmark & Estonia Atria Russia Research and Development Financial Statements and Corporate Governance Financial Statements and Corporate Governance Auditor’s report Corporate Governance Statement Investor reporting Contact information Atria’s Annual Report 2020 Atria Sweden’s net sales were EUR 300.8 million (EUR 289.4 million).
[p.048] Net sales grew by 3.1% in local currency compared to the corresponding period the year before.
[p.048] The coronavirus restrictions had a negative impact on the Food Service and fast food business.
[p.048] On the other hand, sales to the retail sector grew considerably.
[p.048] This had a positive effect on the full-year net sales.
[p.048] The good sales of poultry products strengthened net sales.
[p.048] EBIT was EUR -2.0 million (EUR -6.1 million).
[p.048] EBIT was burdened by decreased sales to fast food and Food Service customers.
[p.048] In addition, the coronavirus pandemic resulted in extra costs.
[p.048] Their impact on the result was mitigated by the compensation for sick leaves paid by the state.
[p.048] Improved efficiency, lower costs and the strengthening of the Swedish krona improved profitability.
[p.048] EBIT for the comparative period includes EUR 1.4 million of costs related to personnel arrangements.
[p.048] Atria Denmark & Estonia’s full-year net sales were EUR 106.8 million (EUR 96.6 million).

[p.048] Net sales grew by 3.0% in local currency.
[p.048] EBIT was EUR -2.9 million (EUR -4.0 million).
[p.048] Sales to the retail sector were significantly higher than in the year before.
[p.048] Sales of the Casademont products grew strongly throughout the review period.
[p.048] Sales of Food Service products declined due to the coronavirus restrictions, but recovered during the fourth quarter.
[p.048] The growth in EBIT was the result of increased net sales and a better sales structure.
[p.048] Events after the period under review After the review period, Atria concluded the sale of its Russian subsidiary Pit-Product to Limited Liability Company Agricultural Complex Mikhailovskiy, which belongs to the Cherkizovo Group.
[p.048] Cherkizovo is Russia’s leading meat products manufacturer and a listed company on the Moscow Stock Exchange since 2006.
[p.048] OOO Pit-Product is a wholly owned subsidiary.
[p.048] Atria has owned the company since 2005.
[p.048] At the end of 2020, the company had approximately 700 employees.
[p.048] The company produces food products for the retail and Food Service channels and owns the Gorelovo and Sinyavino plants.
[p.048] The sale transaction does not include Atria Russia’s subsidiary Sibylla Rus LLC, which conducts fast food business in Russia.
[p.048] The transaction is expected to close during the first half of 2021.
[p.048] The transaction is subject to the approval of the Russian Competition Authority.
[p.048] The impact of the divested business on Atria Group’s net sales is approximately EUR 35 million.
[p.048] The business has been loss-making.
[p.048] The amount of accumulated translation differences related to Pit-Product on December 31, 2020 was EUR -45 million.
[p.048] The translation difference has arisen from exchange rate changes during Pit-Product’s ownership.
[p.048] Atria acquired Pit-Product in 2005.
[p.048] At that time, the exchange rate of the Ruble against the euro was about 34 and at the end of 2020 about 92.
[p.048] Upon divestment of a foreign subsidiary, the accumulated translation differences related to that subsidiary, presented already earlier in equity, are recognized in profit or loss.
[p.048] As the accumulated translation differences already reduce the Group’s equity, this entry will not have an effect on the Group’s equity nor cash flow.
[p.048] Translation differences are not recognized until the final completion of the transaction.
[p.048] The final purchase price will be determined at the closing of the transaction and the divestment is not expected to have any other significant effect on the consolidated result.
[p.048] After the review period, Atria announced the launch of an investment plan to reorganise Atria Sweden’s production lines and to increase productivity.
[p.048] The investment is estimated to total around EUR 30 million.
[p.048] The investment plan will thoroughly investigate the reorganisation of production lines, potential transfers and investment needs related to the construction of new production lines.
[p.048] The project will involve assessing the option of moving production from the Malmö plant to the Sköllersta plant.
[p.048] After the planning phase, the implementation of the investment will be decided on.
[p.048] If implemented, the project is expected to be fully completed during 2023.

[p.048] Euro-denominated short-term Euribors and 1–7-year long-term interest rates were negative throughout the review period.
[p.048] Sweden’s short-term Stibor rates fluctuated on both sides of zero over the year, but the longer-term SEK rates fluctuated between 0–1%.
[p.048] The coronavirus pandemic resulted in significant changes in the financial markets.
[p.048] Liquidity in short-term commercial paper markets declined significantly and the availability of financing became more uncertain as many companies wanted to increase their cash funds at the same time as investors became more cautious and some investors pulled out of the market altogether for a certain period of time.
[p.048] Atria nevertheless managed to refinance its maturing commercial papers with new ones.
[p.048] The pandemic also had an REPORT BY THE BOARD OF DIRECTORS 1 JANUARY–31 DECEMBER 2020 49
[p.049] Front page Atria in brief Atria’s key indicators CEO’s review Strategy 2021–2025 Strategy 2016–2020 Operating environment Business area reviews Atria Finland Atria Sweden Atria Denmark & Estonia Atria Russia Research and Development Financial Statements and Corporate Governance Financial Statements and Corporate Governance Auditor’s report Corporate Governance Statement Investor reporting Contact information Atria’s Annual Report 2020 REPORT BY THE BOARD OF DIRECTORS 1 JANUARY–31 DECEMBER 2020 effect on longer-term loan markets.
[p.049] Banks shortened the maturities of the loans granted and increased margins due to the increased risks attributable to the pandemic.
[p.049] In September, Atria refinanced a EUR 30 million loan, which would have matured in June 2022, with a new EUR 30 million seven-year bullet loan.
[p.049] The Group’s liquidity remained good and is secured through undrawn committed credit facilities of EUR 85 million, which were not used at all during the review period, and a EUR 200 million commercial paper programme, which was used actively for short-term financing.
[p.049] The Group’s net interest rate expenses continued to decrease and were EUR 4.5 million (31 December 2019: 5.6 million).
[p.049] At the end of the financial period, fixed-interest debts represented 16.7% (31 December 2019: 16.0%) of the Group’s entire debt portfolio.
[p.049] Research and product development Atria’s main product groups are fresh and consumer-packed meat, poultry products, convenience foods and meat products, such as sausages and cold cuts.
[p.049] Atria seeks to serve its stakeholders by making extensive use of research and product development in its business operations to further improve current products and develop new ones.
[p.049] Atria’s expertise in market changes and consumer research is integrated into all commercial processes.
[p.049] Market and consumer insight is an integral part of strategy work, product development, marketing and sales.
[p.049] This insight consists of both figures and connective qualitative data.
[p.049] Atria Finland has a high level of market intelligence and the company aims to improve the usability of this intelligence continuously for the processes of product development, sales and marketing.
[p.049] From the perspective of the entire Finnish food industry, one could say that the level and structure of the food service market intelligence lags considerably behind the retail sector intelligence.
[p.049] During 2020, Atria developed studies aiming for a better understanding of particularly the food service market.
[p.049] Atria’s chef barometer (Kokkibarometri), completed in late 2020, sheds an entirely new light on the perceptions and experiences of restaurant professionals in the food service market.
[p.049] Atria Finland launched more than 80 new products in 2020.
[p.049] New products represented 5.6% of total product sales in 2020.
[p.049] The seasoning packets, brought to the market in time for summer, made meat easier to marinate and also reduced the carbon footprint of the packaging.
[p.049] In the autumn, the Artesaani ready-to-eat meals, composed of high-quality ingredients, the one-pan chicken requiring 15 minutes of cooking and the strips of the Murea & Nopea product family made busy everyday life slightly easier.
[p.049] Atria Finland was the first meat processing company to furnish the consumer packaging of its poultry products with a label on each product’s carbon footprint.
[p.049] The first products to carry a carbonfootprint label were poultry products from the Alatalo farm, and they were brought to stores in December 2020.
[p.049] Atria Finland’s consumer packaging will also begin to carry, in phases, easy-to-read recycling instructions which will help consumers sort and recycle product packaging in the correct way.
[p.049] Atria Sweden brought 126 new brand products to the market in 2020.
[p.049] These products represented 3.4% of net sales.
[p.049] All new products, including private label products, accounted for 4.0% of total sales.
[p.049] The most successful new products in 2020 were the Lönneberga poultry products.
[p.049] The adjustment of the food service product range to the change in demand brought about by the coronavirus pandemic was successful.
[p.049] The Atria Denmark & Estonia business area launched a total of 62 new products..
[p.049] Atria holds an approximately 17% market share in the product category of cold cuts in Denmark.
[p.049] In 2020, Atria introduced 11 new brand products in Denmark’s retail sector.
[p.049] Atria Denmark’s most successful new product in 2020 was Aalbæk Specialiteter’s sliced beef salami.
[p.049] In Denmark, new products represented 6.0% of total product sales.
[p.049] In 2020, Atria brought 51 new products to the Estonian market.
[p.049] This represents 7.3% of total sales.
[p.049] The most significant investment in product innovations was the replacement of the traditional minced meat packaging with new environmentally friendly packaging.
[p.049] Thanks to the new minced meat packaging, the amount of packaging material reduced by around 53 tonnes and increased minced meat sales by 43%.
[p.049] In terms of product development, the main focus was on expanding the product categories for healthy food and convenience food.
[p.049] The product range was complemented with poultry products and deep-fried readyto-eat products, for example.
[p.049] Atria Russia launched 43 new products in 2020.
[p.049] Most of the new products were food service products.
[p.049] The product range aimed at retail sector customers was expanded primarily with the Casademont products.
[p.049] The soft Sobrasada sausage and the quality snack product Bocaditos are examples of an entirely new type of product in Russia’s meat product market.
[p.049] The Sibylla brand was also expanded with new products, including tortillas, ready-to-eat hot dogs and helix-shaped grill sausages.
[p.049] The sales of new products accounted for 5.1% of total sales in 2020.

[p.050] Front page Atria in brief Atria’s key indicators CEO’s review Strategy 2021–2025 Strategy 2016–2020 Operating environment Business area reviews Atria Finland Atria Sweden Atria Denmark & Estonia Atria Russia Research and Development Financial Statements and Corporate Governance Financial Statements and Corporate Governance Auditor’s report Corporate Governance Statement Investor reporting Contact information Atria’s Annual Report 2020 Business risks during the review period and short-term risks The coronavirus (COVID-19) pandemic was Atria’s most significant risk in 2020.
[p.050] The social, market economy and public health impact of the pandemic has been visible in Atria’s operations since March 2020.
[p.050] The risk’s significance has varied both in terms of business areas and seasons.
[p.050] The news concerning the vaccines received during the fourth quarter did not yet have the chance to reduce the risk.
[p.050] Instead, the virus’s capacity for mutation resulted in increased coronavirus restrictions and protective measures in some countries.
[p.050] Throughout the pandemic, Atria has invested in ensuring its employees’ health and working capacity as well as in maintaining production reliability.
[p.050] Atria’s different units have adjusted their operations according to the changed circumstances and product demand.
[p.050] Although Atria has incurred some extra costs due to hygiene requirements and the adjustment of operations, the impact on the result and cash flow has been moderate.
[p.050] The company’s financial position has also remained good.
[p.050] Governments have stimulated the economy with support measures and stimulus packages during the pandemic.
[p.050] In Finland, Atria’s operations were supported by a 2.6% reduction in the employer’s pension insurance contributions during the period between 1 May – 31 December 2020.
[p.050] In Sweden, the state compensated companies for sick leaves.
[p.050] The vaccination programmes in different countries got underway in early 2021.
[p.050] The duration of these programmes, the efficacy of various vaccines and the virus’s capacity for rapid mutation nevertheless mean that forecasting the pandemic’s effects on Atria’s 2021 result, balance sheet and cash flow is still difficult.
[p.050] Atria’s normal food production risks pertain to the quality, availability, safety and price of its raw materials and products.
[p.050] The African swine fever occurring in a number of European countries as well as in China and Russia has had an impact on the price as well as the demand and supply of pork around the world.
[p.050] Given that there is a risk of the African swine fever spreading to Finland, Atria has implemented measures aiming to prevent its spread in its own production plants and contract production farms.
[p.050] The cases of avian influenza found in Europe in late 2020, on the other hand, resulted in uncertainty in poultry markets.
[p.050] Information security issues became the subject of increasing public debate during the second half of 2020.
[p.050] Atria’s operations could also become the target of spoofing, hacking or data leakages.
[p.050] The company aims to prevent and protect itself against these risks by systematic monitoring and measures aiming to improve information security.
[p.050] Atria’s personnel is a vitally important resource for the company.
[p.050] Personnel risks are managed with the help of training and preventive measures investing in the safety of work and the personnel’s healthcare.
[p.050] These measures aim to ensure the personnel’s well-being and competence as well as the implementation of Atria’s strategy and the achievement of its goals.
[p.050] Risks and risk management The implementation of Atria’s strategy, the achievement of its goals and responsible operations call for the identification and management of favourable and unfavourable events that affect operations.
[p.050] Favourable events improve Atria’s result and financial position, while unfavourable events increase costs and hinder operations.
[p.050] Atria seeks to prevent unfavourable events and their impact on business operations through risk management as part of its day-to-day operations.
[p.050] Atria’s risk management policy and process guidelines determine goals, principles, responsibilities and authorisations for risk management, as well as operating methods for risk assessment and reporting.
[p.050] More information about Atria’s framework for risk management is available in the Corporate Governance Statement section of the Annual Report.
[p.050] For the purposes of reporting, Atria divides the risks affecting its operations into four categories: strategic, operational, liability and financial risks.
[p.050] Strategic risks relate to operational development and the planning and implementation of long-term business decisions as well as to brands, management systems, the allocation of resources and the ability to respond to changes in the operating environment.
[p.050] Atria’s Board of Directors participates in the identification and management of strategic risks.
[p.050] Operational risks are related to day-to-day business operations in processes, systems and people’s activities, for example.
[p.050] Everyone at Atria participates in the identification and management of these risks.
[p.050] Liability risks are errors, malfunctions and accidents that occur within Atria or in the business environment and that cause damage or loss.
[p.050] Liability risks are managed through continuity plans, and Atria seeks to transfer them to insurance companies.
[p.050] Financial risks have to do with changes in market prices and the sufficiency of financial assets in the short and medium terms as well as to counterparties’ ability to meet their financial obligations.
[p.050] Financial risks are managed in cooperation with financial institutions and by making use of various financial instruments in minimising risks.
[p.050] REPORT BY THE BOARD OF DIRECTORS 1 JANUARY–31 DECEMBER 2020 51
[p.051] Front page Atria in brief Atria’s key indicators CEO’s review Strategy 2021–2025 Strategy 2016–2020 Operating environment Business area reviews Atria Finland Atria Sweden Atria Denmark & Estonia Atria Russia Research and Development Financial Statements and Corporate Governance Financial Statements and Corporate Governance Auditor’s report Corporate Governance Statement Investor reporting Contact information Atria’s Annual Report 2020 REPORT BY THE BOARD OF DIRECTORS 1 JANUARY–31 DECEMBER 2020 The following table presents a brief summary of the most significant risks related to Atria’s operations.
[p.051] Individually or combined, these risks may have favourable or unfavourable impacts on Atria’s business operations, result, financial position, competitiveness and reputation.
[p.051] The risks shown in the table are presented in random order.
[p.051] Risks related to raw materials and their production Risk description Risk management Fluctuation in the demand for meat, animal diseases, extreme weather phenomena as well as changes in the rearing costs and capacity of contract producers have an impact on the purchase prices of the meat raw materials.
[p.051] Atria steers the purchasing of meat raw materials centrally and relies on a wide network of suppliers in the purchasing.
[p.051] Contract producers are furthermore guided in rearing and animal care.
[p.051] The quality of raw materials and products and safety in the entire production chain are of primary importance to Atria.
[p.051] Atria ensures the safety of its production processes every day and checks that various microbiological, chemical and physical risk factors are eliminated.
[p.051] Product safety is ensured in accordance with operating methods required by food safety management and quality certifications.
[p.051] The chickens and pigs on Atria Family Farms are raised without antibiotics.
[p.051] The name of the Family Farm – that is, the origin of the meat – is indicated on the product packaging.
[p.051] Food consumption and production has an environmental impact.
[p.051] Among other things, the food production chain has an impact on global warming, the eutrophication and acidification of the environment as well as the loss of biodiversity.
[p.051] In addition, it consumes nutrients, land areas, energy and water resources.
[p.051] Environmental impacts and climate change as well as efforts to combat them may have effects on Atria’s operations, result and reputation.
[p.051] Such effects may include changes in consumption and business processes, material damage, the need for technological changes, increased regulation and heavier environmental taxation.
[p.051] In accordance with its environmental policy, Atria works systematically to minimise its environmental impact.
[p.051] Atria is committed to reducing its carbon dioxide emissions and other environmental impacts both in its own production and across the food chain, from the field to the table.
[p.051] A carbon-neutral food chain by 2035 is Atria’s most important goal In-depth knowledge of the food chain and its environmental impacts is crucial for Atria.
[p.051] The company engages in close cooperation with research institutions and other industry operators.
[p.051] In addition, Atria requires its partners to operate in an environmentally responsible manner.
[p.051] Atria’s environmental impact is managed in many ways: by increasing energy efficiency, using renewable energy sources to an increasing degree, reducing waste, developing ecological packaging solutions, and using water and other natural resources responsibly.
[p.051] In addition to ensuring that its operations meet the statutory requirements, Atria promotes the development and adoption of new technologies.
[p.051] The health and welfare of animals is important for Atria.
[p.051] An animal disease at a critical point in Atria’s production chain could interrupt production in the unit concerned and disrupt operations throughout the chain.
[p.051] Animal diseases may also result in export and import restrictions imposed on meat products.
[p.051] Atria ensures animal welfare with quality requirements pertaining to production and purchasing contracts.
[p.051] Atria’s multi-stage self-monitoring aims to detect potential hazards related to animal health and welfare as early as possible.
[p.051] In Finland, contract production and the related production guidelines for each species, as well as traceability, are one of the key aspects of monitoring and further improving the welfare of Atria’s production animals.
[p.051] Atria’s contract producers have comprehensive group animal disease insurance to minimise the impacts of any damage to producers.
[p.051] 52
[p.052] Front page Atria in brief Atria’s key indicators CEO’s review Strategy 2021–2025 Strategy 2016–2020 Operating environment Business area reviews Atria Finland Atria Sweden Atria Denmark & Estonia Atria Russia Research and Development Financial Statements and Corporate Governance Financial Statements and Corporate Governance Auditor’s report Corporate Governance Statement Investor reporting Contact information Atria’s Annual Report 2020 Risks related to the geographical area of operation and markets Risk description Risk management The retail trade in the food industry is centralised in Atria’s most important market areas.
[p.052] This enables Atria to develop and diversify its long-term cooperation with customers.
[p.052] On the other hand, a change in the operations of an individual customer may have a bigger impact on Atria’s operations.
[p.052] In risk management, Atria makes use of its good customer cooperation, well-known brands, efficient industrial processes, high-quality products and financial monitoring.
[p.052] Changes in consumer behaviour may have an impact on both the short-term and long-term demand for Atria’s products.
[p.052] Health aspects, animal welfare, ethical considerations and climate change are examples of factors that may affect consumer behaviour.
[p.052] Changes in consumer behaviour may have positive or negative impacts on Atria’s profitability and the reputation of its brands.
[p.052] Atria is preparing for changes in demand and consumption habits and the need to adapt its operations by investing in consumer-oriented and sustainable product development.
[p.052] In addition, Atria informs consumers about its products, its own operations and its responsibility.
[p.052] Competitors’ operations and product selections, as well as private labels, affect Atria’s profitability.
[p.052] Atria develops its product range from a customer-driven perspective, monitors market changes actively, ensures the efficiency of operations, maintains good delivery reliability and invests in informative consumer marketing.
[p.052] Atria’s geographical area of operation exposes the company to risks related to the national economy, legislation and official regulations in various countries.
[p.052] Global geopolitical risks, pandemics and animal diseases may also have an effect on Atria’s operations.
[p.052] Atria manages the risk with contracts and by monitoring amendments to legislation and investing in quality matters.
[p.052] Atria also trains its personnel, relies on the services of experts and conducts audits.
[p.052] Personnel risks Risk description Risk management The availability of competent and motivated employees is a risk for Atria’s strategy implementation and the achievement of its goals.
[p.052] Atria invests in employee development and training through a wide range of training opportunities.
[p.052] Development needs are also identified through employee surveys.
[p.052] Epidemics and pandemics have an impact on the personnel’s health.
[p.052] Health risks are managed with the help of training and preventive measures investing in the safety of work, protective clothing and masks and the personnel’s healthcare.
[p.052] Low temperatures and repetitive movements are characteristic of work in the food industry.
[p.052] The work is often physically demanding and involves cutting machines and tools.
[p.052] This increases the risk of occupational accidents.
[p.052] Atria aims to prevent occupational accidents, the risks of occupational disease and the related costs by investing significantly in safety at work.

[p.053] Front page Atria in brief Atria’s key indicators CEO’s review Strategy 2021–2025 Strategy 2016–2020 Operating environment Business area reviews Atria Finland Atria Sweden Atria Denmark & Estonia Atria Russia Research and Development Financial Statements and Corporate Governance Financial Statements and Corporate Governance Auditor’s report Corporate Governance Statement Investor reporting Contact information Atria’s Annual Report 2020 REPORT BY THE BOARD OF DIRECTORS 1 JANUARY–31 DECEMBER 2020 Risks related to information management Risk description Risk management The automation of operational processes, information systems and digitalisation have increased risks related to the accessibility, functionality, integrity, availability, reliability, identifiability and authentication of operations and services.
[p.053] Atria aims to minimise information security risks and accelerate the recovery from such risks with continuous and systematic monitoring.
[p.053] The company also conducts risk assessments in relation to its personnel, data communications, software, hardware, accessibility and physical security.
[p.053] Atria also relies on external experts in the management of information security risks.
[p.053] A failure to protect personal data or other important data may damage the company’s reputation and result in financial sanctions and/or liability for damages.
[p.053] Atria pays special attention to information security through technical protection and audits, and by providing employees with training and guidelines.
[p.053] Liability risks Risk description Risk management Unforeseeable liability risks at Atria’s production plants in Finland, Sweden, Denmark, Estonia or Russia may interrupt operations at a production plant.
[p.053] All Atria’s production plants are insured against any physical damage and interruptions in operations through the Group’s insurance policies.
[p.053] A risk analysis is prepared annually or every two years at key plants.
[p.053] Continuity planning is in place to limit the potential damage caused by business interruptions.
[p.053] Financial risks Risk description Risk management Key risks related to financing in Atria’s operations include currency transaction and translation risks, the interest rate risk, and the liquidity and refinancing risk.
[p.053] The goal of financial risk management is to reduce the impact of price fluctuations in financial markets and other uncertainty factors on earnings, the balance sheet and cash flow, in addition to ensuring sufficient liquidity.
[p.053] Note 29 to the financial statements contains more detailed information on Atria’s management of financial risks.
[p.053] Atria’s risk management has mapped risks related to human rights, corruption and bribery.
[p.053] None of these risks have been detected or materialised in Atria’s operations.
[p.053] To prevent risks of this kind in the future as well, Atria maintains partnership principles and a purchasing policy.
[p.053] The implementation of these principles and the policy are monitored with the help of assessments and audits.
[p.053] The personnel is also trained to identify and report such risks.

[p.055] Front page Atria in brief Atria’s key indicators CEO’s review Strategy 2021–2025 Strategy 2016–2020 Operating environment Business area reviews Atria Finland Atria Sweden Atria Denmark & Estonia Atria Russia Research and Development Financial Statements and Corporate Governance Financial Statements and Corporate Governance Auditor’s report Corporate Governance Statement Investor reporting Contact information Atria’s Annual Report 2020 REPORT BY THE BOARD OF DIRECTORS 1 JANUARY–31 DECEMBER 2020 Incentive schemes for management and key personnel Long-term share-based incentive scheme 2018–2020 In 2017, Atria Plc’s Board of Directors decided on the long-term incentive scheme for key personnel for 2018–2020.
[p.055] The share-based incentive scheme aimed to encourage Atria’s management to acquire company shares, as well as to increase the company’s value through their decisions and actions over the long term.
[p.055] The scheme, based on a shares and a cash bonus, is divided into three one-year periods.
[p.055] The third earning period began on 1 January 2020 and ended on 31 December 2020.
[p.055] The possible bonus in the scheme is based on the company’s earnings per share (70%) and organic growth (30%).
[p.055] The bonuses for the 2020 earning period are paid in three equal instalments in 2021, 2022 and 2023, partly as company shares and partly in cash.
[p.055] The cash proportion aims to cover any taxes and tax-like payments incurred by the person due to the bonus.
[p.055] If the person’s employment relationship or service contract ends prior to the payment of the bonus, the bonus is not usually paid.
[p.055] The share-based incentive scheme covers a maximum of 40 people.
[p.055] The bonuses to be paid for the 2020 earning period are estimated at EUR 0.9 million.
[p.055] The concluded long-term incentive scheme Payments for the 2015–2017 earning period were based on the Group’s earnings per share (EPS), excluding extraordinary items.
[p.055] The cash bonuses payable under the scheme for the 2015–2017 earning period were capped at EUR 4.5 million.
[p.055] The scheme ended on 31 December 2017, and it covered a maximum of 45 people, including the CEO, the Group’s Management Team and the management teams of the business areas.
[p.055] The bonuses accrued for the 2015–2017 earning period totalled EUR 2.1 million.
[p.055] The final bonus instalment was paid in March 2020 and it amounted to EUR 0.2 million.
[p.055] Short-term incentive scheme The maximum bonus payable under Atria Plc’s short-term incentive plan is 25–50% of the annual salary, depending on the performance impact and requirement level of each individual’s role.
[p.055] The criteria in the bonus scheme are the performance requirements and net sales at Group level and in the individual’s area of responsibility.
[p.055] In addition to the CEO and other members of the Group’s Management Team, Atria Plc’s bonus schemes cover around 40 people.
[p.055] New long-term incentive scheme for 2021–2023 Atria Plc’s Board of Directors has decided on a long-term incentive scheme for key personnel for 2021–2023.
[p.055] The scheme is basically identical to the scheme for 2018–2020.
[p.055] The new scheme, based on a shares and a cash bonus, is divided into three one-year periods, with the first earning period beginning on 1 January 2021 and ending on 31 December 2021.
[p.055] The bonuses for the 2021 earning period are paid in three equal parts in 2022, 2023 and 2024, partly as company’s exchange shares and partly in cash.
[p.055] The cash proportion aims to cover any taxes and tax-like payments incurred by the person due to the bonus.
[p.055] If the person’s employment relationship or service contract ends prior to the payment of the bonus, the bonus is not usually paid.
[p.055] The share-based incentive scheme covers a maximum of 40 people.
[p.055] The maximum value of the bonuses to be paid on the basis of one earning period is EUR 2 million.
[p.055] The new incentive scheme aims to encourage Atria’s management to acquire company shares and to enhance the company’s long-term increase in value by their decisions and activities.
[p.055] Outlook for 2021 Atria Group’s adjusted EBIT in 2021 is expected to be EUR 37–43 million (EUR 40.5 million).
[p.055] The adjusted EBIT is determined by adjusting the EBIT recognised in the income statement for items materially affecting comparability.
[p.055] These may include events that are not part of ordinary business activities, such as the restructuring of operations, capital gains and losses attributable to the sale of operations, impairment, and the costs of discontinuing significant operations.
[p.055] If materialised, the translation difference recognised as a result of the disposal of OOO Pit-Product would be such an item with an effect on the result.
[p.055] The translation differences related to Pit-Product accumulated by 31 December 2020 were approximately EUR -45 million.
[p.055] The recognised translation differences depend on the development of the exchange rate of the Russian rouble and they will be recognised when the deal is closed.
[p.055] Atria operates mainly in retail and food service markets in Finland and Sweden.
[p.055] Significant and sudden changes in the global meat market are having an increasingly strong impact on the company’s development, in addition to reducing predictability.
[p.055] The consumption of poultry is expected to further increase, while the consumption red meat is expected to decrease slightly.
[p.055] Atria has increased its export of meat, and pork exports to China, for example, are expected to continue to grow in 2021.
[p.055] The coronavirus pandemic which emerged in 2020 and was still present at the beginning of 2021 has resulted in strong and rapid changes in the food industry’s operating environment.
[p.055] This has made forecasting of the company’s development more difficult.
[p.055] Direct impacts on Atria’s business include the national restrictions imposed on restaurant activities and public food services, which reduce sales to Food Service customers.
[p.055] The importance of everyday meals has grown during the pandemic.
[p.055] Any possible deterioration in consumers’ purchasing power would also have an impact on grocery purchases and could prove unfavourable in terms of the sales of Atria’s products.
