[p.056] Atria Plc’s share capital The parent company’s share capital is distributed as follows: • Series A shares (1 vote per share) 19,063,747 shares • Series KII shares (10 votes per share) 9,203,981 shares Series A shares have a right of priority to a dividend of EUR 0.17, after which series KII shares are paid a dividend of up to EUR 0.17.
[p.056] If distributable dividends remain after this, series A and series KII shares entitle their holders to an equal right to a dividend.
[p.056] Atria’s Articles of Association include a pre-emptive purchase clause concerning series KII shares.
[p.056] If series KII shares are transferred to a party outside the company or to a shareholder within the company who has not previously owned series KII shares, the proposed recipient of the shares must inform the Board of Directors about this without delay, and KII shareholders have the right to pre-emptively purchase the shares under certain conditions.
[p.056] In addition, the acquisition of series KII shares by means of transfer requires the approval of the company.
[p.056] Series A shares have no such limitations.
[p.056] At the end of the financial period on 31 December 2020, the company held a total of 105,311 treasury shares, representing 0.4% of the shares and 0.1% of the votes in the company.

[p.057] Front page Atria in brief Atria’s key indicators CEO’s review Strategy 2021–2025 Strategy 2016–2020 Operating environment Business area reviews Atria Finland Atria Sweden Atria Denmark & Estonia Atria Russia Research and Development Financial Statements and Corporate Governance Financial Statements and Corporate Governance Auditor’s report Corporate Governance Statement Investor reporting Contact information Atria’s Annual Report 2020 REPORT BY THE BOARD OF DIRECTORS 1 JANUARY–31 DECEMBER 2020 The Board of Directors will propose to the Annual General Meeting that the distributable funds be used as follows: • a dividend of EUR 0.50 per share be paid, totalling EUR 14,087,771.50 • to be retained as equity, EUR 253,672,898.05 267,760,669.55 Statement on non-financial information Securing a sustainable food chain Corporate responsibility is an integral part of Atria’s business and corporate culture.
[p.057] Responsibility is integrated into all levels of Atria’s operations: its mission, goals, values, operating strategies, management and day-to-day work.
[p.057] Through its responsible operations, the company aims to secure its current and future operating conditions.
[p.057] In line with the principles of sustainable development, the company considers the economic, social and environmental aspects of its operations in all its business areas.
[p.057] Atria’s chain of good food consists of primary production and the purchasing of raw materials, industrial production, customers and consumers.
[p.057] The food chain takes into account value creation and distribution at the various stages of production, the environmental impacts, and the social impacts related to the food chain and products.
[p.057] The planet, food and people are Atria’s material sustainability focuses for the development and implementation of responsible business operations.
[p.057] By investing in the development of corporate responsibility matters relevant to Atria, the company secures its future operating conditions and creates both financial and social value to society.
[p.057] Direct financial value arises from the jobs provided by Atria, and indirect value from the supply chain and taxes paid.
[p.057] Social value is created by developing the industry in line with the principles of sustainable development and producing food for the needs of customers and consumers with the help of trustworthy brands and a trustworthy corporate image.
[p.057] Atria actively seeks to make an impact on society through trade associations.
[p.057] Atria’s corporate responsibility is managed at two levels.
[p.057] In Atria Group’s new strategy for 2021–2025, the company states its goal of of leader in sustainability.
[p.057] Concrete goals include a carbon-neutral food chain by 2035, increasing the production of antibioticfree meat production and a reduction in carbon dioxide emissions.
[p.057] The shared Code of Conduct and policies are determined at Group level.
[p.057] The Group also ensures compliance with the Code and the policies, and determines the development projects and strategic target state applicable to all business areas.
[p.057] The annual reporting related to Atria’s corporate responsibility is also implemented at Group level.
[p.057] The realisation and continuous improvement of Atria’s responsibility are part of day-to-day operational management across the business areas.
[p.057] The steering groups of the business areas analyse the operating environment and key stakeholders’ expectations with regard to responsibility, and also integrate the implementation of the necessary development measures into their business plans.
[p.057] Stakeholders are strongly present in the food chain, from raw material procurement all the way to the finished products and their use.
[p.057] Listening to stakeholders and taking their needs into account is one of the cornerstones of Atria’s sustainability work.
[p.057] Atria’s responsibility is constructed through dialogue and is supported by openness and transparency.
[p.057] Atria’s Corporate Responsibility Report contains a comprehensive description of the company’s sustainability work.
[p.057] The Corporate Responsibility Report is available on Atria’s website at https://www.atria.fi/en/group/corporate-responsibility/corporate-responsibility-reporting/.
[p.057] Atria’s reporting is based on the international Global Reporting Initiative (GRI) standard.
[p.057] Atria has selected the essential measurements and indicators relevant to its operations and stakeholders from the GRI standard.
[p.057] The Atria Code of Conduct supports sustainable business operations Compliance with healthy and sustainable business practices lays the foundation for Atria’s operations.
[p.057] The Atria Code of Conduct is a set of ethical principles concerning business operations, stakeholder relations and environmental responsibility, approved by Atria Plc’s Board of Directors.
[p.057] The Code of Conduct is supported by internal policies and guidelines that define and guide operating methods.
[p.057] The Code of Conduct concerns all Atria employees in all business areas.
[p.057] The Atria Code of Conduct and the corporate policies supporting the Code are based on the laws and collective agreements of Atria’s countries of operation, and on international agreements and recommendations concerning responsible operations in terms of human rights and anti-corruption, for example.
[p.057] In accordance with its Code of Conduct, Atria has zero tolerance for any type of corruption or bribery.
[p.057] Atria’s employees must not give or receive benefits, gifts or hospitality that could inappropriately influence business decisions.
[p.057] Atria’s employees have been familiarised with the Code of Conduct and the policies that support the Code through an induction programme that supports their job descriptions.
[p.057] Respect for human rights is an integral part of Atria’s Code of Conduct and HR policy.
[p.057] Atria respects and supports internationally recognised human rights principles and requires all its employees, suppliers and subcontractors to comply with these principles.
[p.057] Through its Code of Conduct and the policies that support the Code, Atria is committed to the following international agreements and recommendations: • UN Universal Declaration of Human Rights and Convention on Rights of the Child • UN Global Compact initiative for the promotion of human rights, labour rights, environmental protection and the prevention of corruption • ILO Declaration on Fundamental Principles and Rights at Work • OECD Guidelines for Multinational Enterprises 58
[p.058] Front page Atria in brief Atria’s key indicators CEO’s review Strategy 2021–2025 Strategy 2016–2020 Operating environment Business area reviews Atria Finland Atria Sweden Atria Denmark & Estonia Atria Russia Research and Development Financial Statements and Corporate Governance Financial Statements and Corporate Governance Auditor’s report Corporate Governance Statement Investor reporting Contact information Atria’s Annual Report 2020 • Business Charter for Sustainable Development of the International Chamber of Commerce (ICC) and the ICC Rules on Combating Corruption • Responsible purchasing principles of the Business Social Compliance Initiative (BSCI) Atria expects its business partners to comply with either their own code of conduct or the equivalent Atria Partnership Code of Conduct within their operations.
[p.058] In addition, procurement contracts obligate Atria’s partners to meet the company’s requirements for product quality, operating methods and the supply chain, for example.
[p.058] Atria assesses the compliance of its contractual partners’ operations before undertaking a partnership and on a regular basis during the partnership.
[p.058] In addition to the experience gained during the business relationship, the assessment takes into account risk factors related to financial, environmental and social responsibility.
[p.058] Atria has the right to audit the operations of its contractual partners if necessary.
[p.058] In the audits, attention is paid to food safety, for example, as well as environmental and social responsibility, such as human rights and the prevention of corruption and bribery.
[p.058] Atria has established a whistleblowing channel for its employees to report suspected breaches of the Code of Conduct or illegal activities.
[p.058] All reports are processed confidentially, and Atria implements any necessary measures based on the reports.
[p.058] The related indicator is the number of reports submitted to the whistleblowing channel or to the authorities.
[p.058] No reports were submitted to Atria’s whistleblowing channel during 2020.
[p.058] PLANET In accordance with its environmental policy, Atria works systematically to minimise its environmental impact.
[p.058] Atria is committed to reducing carbon dioxide emissions and other environmental impacts in its own production and across the food chain.
[p.058] The goals of environmental management at Atria’s plants have been adjusted to changes in the operating environment.
[p.058] Priorities include energy efficiency, water efficiency and the prevention of waste and food waste, as well as ensuring statutory compliance in operations.
[p.058] Concerning the food chain as a whole, a carbon-neutral food chain by 2035 is Atria’s most important environmental goal.
[p.058] The means and measures for achieving a carbon-neutral food chain and the key indicators of environmental responsibility are reported in more detail in the Corporate Responsibility Report.
[p.058] Producers play a key role in mitigating the environmental impact of primary production.
[p.058] At the farm level, minimising environmental impacts means farm-specific solutions based on the type of production.
[p.058] Resource efficiency and good input-output ratios play a key role in terms of the environment.
[p.058] The key projects to improve the environmental efficiency of the production chain are discussed in the business area reviews in the Annual Report and in the Corporate Responsibility Report.
[p.058] Energy Sustainable, efficient energy use reduces carbon dioxide emissions, which facilitate climate change.
[p.058] Atria Group’s energy consumption in 2020 was 514,976 MWh.
[p.058] Consumption decreased by 1.3%, and consumption per kilo produced decreased by 2.8% year-on-year.
[p.058] The decrease in energy consumption was the result of a growth in the share of biofuels at Atria’s plant in Nurmo, Finland, and a general decrease in consumption achieved through energy efficiency measures, particularly in terms of heating energy.
[p.058] Atria Group’s carbon dioxide emissions have decreased by 27% from the 2016 level.
[p.058] The decrease in carbon dioxide emissions was due to the increased use of renewable energy sources, such as increasing the share of bio-based fuels in heat production.
[p.058] Water The quality, adequacy and pumping capacity of water are critical for Atria’s operations.
[p.058] Plant-specific environmental permits determine the threshold values for wastewater quality.
[p.058] All wastewater is directed to a local wastewater treatment facility.
[p.058] Atria Group’s water consumption in 2020 was 3,020,256 m3.
[p.058] Consumption decreased by 1%, and consumption per kilo produced decreased by 2% compared to 2019.
[p.058] The continuous management of water consumption is part of the plants’ environmental management and continuous improvement.
[p.058] Materials Food production is at the core of the circular economy.
[p.058] Side streams that do not end up as products are directed back to the food chain, as precisely and with as high a value as possible.
[p.058] They are used in applications of the feed industry, as nutrients, for material recycling or as energy.
[p.058] During the strategy period which concluded at the end 2020, Atria focused on strengthening an anti-wastage operating culture.
[p.058] Atria’s internal waste management aims to improve value creation for material flows suitable for food production.
[p.058] Atria’s wastage is managed in accordance with the same principles in all business areas of the Group.
[p.058] The various types of process wastage have been identified and monitoring indicators have been created for them.
[p.058] They are displayed at the departments and daily management reacts to deviations without delay.
[p.058] In addition to the personnel’s activities, wastage reduction requires investments in the processes.
[p.058] Compliance The operations of Atria’s production plants are subject to environmental permits.
[p.058] All Atria’s production plants have management systems that meet the requirements of the ISO 14001 standard for environmental systems and the requirements of the ISO 50001 standard for energy management systems.
[p.058] The Corporate Responsibility Report includes information about the system certification status.
[p.058] No leaks were reported, no warnings were issued by the authorities, and no coercive measures were imposed in the reporting period.
[p.058] REPORT BY THE BOARD OF DIRECTORS 1 JANUARY–31 DECEMBER 2020 59
[p.059] Front page Atria in brief Atria’s key indicators CEO’s review Strategy 2021–2025 Strategy 2016–2020 Operating environment Business area reviews Atria Finland Atria Sweden Atria Denmark & Estonia Atria Russia Research and Development Financial Statements and Corporate Governance Financial Statements and Corporate Governance Auditor’s report Corporate Governance Statement Investor reporting Contact information Atria’s Annual Report 2020 PRODUCT Origin Atria’s food is ethically produced, pure and safe.
[p.059] The production chain is open and transparent.
[p.059] Atria is aiming for a fully transparent food chain, where consumers and other parties can be provided with information about the origin of all the raw materials, ingredients and packaging materials that we use.
[p.059] Meat is the most important raw material for Atria’s products.
[p.059] Animal welfare is ensured and proved throughout Atria’s food chain.
[p.059] Environmental considerations related to food production are continuously subject to public debate.
[p.059] Atria wants to lead the way in proving that meat can still be an ethically sustainable choice for consumers as part of well-balanced diets.
[p.059] In the development of sustainable primary production, Atria invests in animal welfare, animal disease management and the development of feeding solutions in cooperation with meat producers, industry experts and research institutions, for example.
[p.059] The good treatment of production animals and animal welfare are key operating principles for Atria.
[p.059] In its operations, Atria complies with the laws related to the treatment and slaughter of animals.
[p.059] More detailed information about this is provided in Atria’s Corporate Responsibility Report.
[p.059] Tuoretie Oy is responsible for Atria Finland’s animal transport operations and compliance with the related laws.
[p.059] These aspects are also reported in more detail in the Corporate Responsibility Report.
[p.059] Safety If materialised, a product safety risk could have fatal consequences for people’s health and Atria’s business operations.
[p.059] Atria therefore takes product safety extremely seriously.
[p.059] Atria’s food safety and quality policy lays the foundation for commitments, goal setting and continuous improvement.
[p.059] The product safety management systems of Atria’s production plants have FSSC 22000 certification.
[p.059] During statutory assessments in 2020, no serious shortcomings in operating methods were detected that could compromise food safety and result in fines or coercive measures imposed by the authorities.
[p.059] In 2020, Atria had to carry out five product recalls.
[p.059] Two in Finland, two in Sweden and one in Estonia.
[p.059] No recalls were necessary in Denmark and Russia.
[p.059] More detailed information about Atria’s principles and results concerning the origin and safe production of food is provided in the Corporate Responsibility Report, starting from page 27 PEOPLE Consumers As a food producer, Atria understands its responsibility towards consumers and public health.
[p.059] The purity and nutritional quality of food, as well as ethical food chains, are important values for consumers.
[p.059] People’s well-being is based on healthy and nourishing food.
[p.059] Atria’s main product categories are fresh and consumer-packed meat and meat products, such as sausages and cold cuts, as well as convenience foods and poultry products.
[p.059] By participating in applied research in product and packaging technology and nutrition, Atria can also create innovative products and concepts for future needs.
[p.059] Further information about the results of Atria’s product development and research operations is provided on page 42.
[p.059] Employees The company’s future relies on highly competent employees and well-being at work.
[p.059] We want to offer a workplace where competent professionals thrive.
[p.059] Our goal is to be one of the most attractive employers in the food industry.
[p.059] Safety at work is one of the cornerstones of our operations: we ensure in many different ways that our employees return safely home from Atria.
[p.059] Our long-term goal is zero accidents across Atria Group.
[p.059] Our HR policy defines the material aspects of personnel responsibility concerning employment relationships.
[p.059] These include a fair employment relationship, well-being and safety at work, competence development, equality, non-discrimination and freedom of association, as well as the prevention of child labour and forced labour.
[p.059] In 2020, Atria Group continued to implement the Safely Home from Atria occupational safety programme.
[p.059] Employees’ well-being improved in 2020, confirmed by sickness absence levels and accident frequency rates.
[p.059] Further information about Atria’s responsibility for people is provided in the Corporate Responsibility Report, starting from page 29.
[p.059] REPORT BY THE BOARD OF DIRECTORS 1 JANUARY–31 DECEMBER 2020 60

[p.063] Front page Atria in brief Atria’s key indicators CEO’s review Strategy 2021–2025 Strategy 2016–2020 Operating environment Business area reviews Atria Finland Atria Sweden Atria Denmark & Estonia Atria Russia Research and Development Financial Statements and Corporate Governance Financial Statements and Corporate Governance Auditor’s report Corporate Governance Statement Investor reporting Contact information Atria’s Annual Report 2020 GROUP’S FINANCIAL INDICATORS FINANCIAL INDICATORS In addition to the IFRS figures, Atria publishes other widely used alternative financial indicators that can be derived from the income statement and balance sheet.
[p.063] Principles for calculating financial indicators: Adjusted EBIT = In addition to reporting EBIT, the company publishes an adjusted EBIT indicator to describe the actual financial development of the business and to improve comparability between different periods.
[p.063] The adjusted EBIT is determined by adjusting the EBIT recognised in the income statement for material items that affect comparability.
[p.063] These may include events that are not part of ordinary business activities, such as the restructuring of operations, capital gains and losses attributable to the sale of operations, impairment, and the costs of discontinuing significant operations.
[p.063] Gross investments = Investments in tangible and intangible assets, including acquired businesses Free cash flow = Cash flow from operating activities - Cash flow from investments FTE = Hours worked during the review period Number of working days during the review period * normal working hours per day Return on equity (%) = Profit/loss for the accounting period * 100 Equity (average) Return on investment % = Profit/loss before tax + interest and other financial expenses * 100 Equity + interest-bearing financial liabilities (average) Equity ratio (%) = Shareholders’ equity * 100 Balance sheet total – advance payments received Interest-bearing liabilities = Loans + lease liabilities Gearing (%) = Interest-bearing liabilities * 100 Shareholders’ equity Net interest-bearing liabilities = Interest-bearing liabilities - cash and cash equivalents Net gearing (%) = Interest-bearing liabilities – cash and cash equivalents * 100 Shareholders’ equity Earnings per share (basic) = Profit for the period attributable to the owners of the parent company Weighted average of outstanding shares Equity/share = Equity attributable to the owners of the parent company Undiluted number of shares on 31 Dec Dividend per share = Dividend distribution during the accounting period Undiluted number of shares on 31 Dec Dividend/profit (%) = Dividend/share * 100 Earnings per share (EPS) Effective dividend yield (%) = Dividend/share * 100 Closing price at the end of the accounting period Price/earnings (P/E) = Closing price at the end of the accounting period Earnings per share Average price = Overall share turnover in euro Undiluted average number of shares traded during the financial period Market capitalisation = Number of shares at the end of the financial period * closing price on 31 Dec Share turnover (%) = Number of shares traded during the accounting period * 100 Undiluted average number of shares 64

[p.067] IFRS FINANCIAL STATEMENTS 68
[p.068] Front page Atria in brief Atria’s key indicators CEO’s review Strategy 2021–2025 Strategy 2016–2020 Operating environment Business area reviews Atria Finland Atria Sweden Atria Denmark & Estonia Atria Russia Research and Development Financial Statements and Corporate Governance Financial Statements and Corporate Governance Auditor’s report Corporate Governance Statement Investor reporting Contact information Atria’s Annual Report 2020 Basic corporate information The parent company of Atria Group, Atria Plc, is a Finnish public limited liability company established in accordance with the laws of Finland and domiciled in Kuopio, Finland.
[p.068] The company has been listed on Nasdaq Helsinki Ltd. since 1991.
[p.068] Copies of the consolidated financial statements are available online at www.atria.com and at the parent company’s head office at Itikanmäenkatu 3, Seinäjoki, Finland; postal address: PO Box 900, 60060 ATRIA, Finland.
[p.068] Atria Plc and its subsidiaries manufacture and market food products, especially meat products, poultry products, meals and food concepts.
[p.068] Atria’s main market area covers Finland, Sweden, Denmark, European Russia and the Baltic countries.
[p.068] Atria’s subsidiaries are also located in this area.
[p.068] Atria Group’s reporting segments are Atria Finland, Atria Sweden, Atria Denmark & Estonia and Atria Russia.
[p.068] The financial statements were approved for publication by the Board of Directors on 18 March 2021.
[p.068] According to the Finnish Limited Liability Companies Act, the shareholders are entitled to approve or reject the financial statements at the Annual General Meeting (AGM) to be held after the publication of the financial statements.
[p.068] The AGM can also decide to revise the financial statements.
[p.068] Accounting policies BASIS OF PREPARATION The consolidated financial statements have been prepared in accordance with the International Financial Reporting Standards (IFRS) adopted the EU.
[p.068] The IAS and IFRS standards valid on 31 December 2020 have been followed, as well as SIC and IFRIC interpretations.
[p.068] The IFRS refer to standards and interpretations approved for application in the EU in compliance with Regulation (EC) 1606/2002, as referred to in the Finnish Accounting Act and subsequent regulations.
[p.068] The notes to the consolidated financial statements also comply with Finnish accounting and corporate legislation.
[p.068] The consolidated financial statements have been prepared on an acquisition cost basis except for biological assets, financial assets recognised at fair value in other comprehensive income, financial assets and liabilities measured at fair value through profit or loss, and derivative financial instruments.
[p.068] From the moment of classification, the assets held for sale are measured at the lower of their balance sheet value and fair value less cost to sell.
[p.068] The financial statement data is presented in thousands of euros, with sums rounded off to the nearest thousand.
[p.068] IMPACTS OF COVID-19, ACCOUNTING POLICIES CALLING FOR MANAGEMENT DISCRETION AND KEY UNCERTAINTY FACTORS RELATED TO ASSESSMENTS When preparing the financial statements, discretion must be used in applying the accounting policies.
[p.068] In addition, the management must make assessments and assumptions that concern the future and affect assets and liabilities in relation to responsibilities, profits and costs.
[p.068] The realised values may deviate from the original assessments and assumptions.
[p.068] The Group’s management makes discretionary decisions regarding the choice and application of accounting policies.
[p.068] This particularly affects cases where the valid IFRS norms include alternative recognition, measurement or presentation procedures.
[p.068] The management has exercised discretion in the valuation and classification of assets and financial items, in the recognition of deferred tax assets and provisions, and in the classification of associated companies and joint ventures as materially significant.
[p.068] The assessments are based on the management’s best estimate at the end date of the reporting period.
[p.068] They are affected by previous experiences and assumptions about the future that are deemed the most likely at the end of the period and are related to the expected developments in the Group’s financial environment.
[p.068] Any changes in the assessments and assumptions are recognised in the accounting period during which the assessment or assumption is adjusted and in all subsequent accounting periods.
[p.068] The exceptional situation resulting from the COVID-19 pandemic, as well as the uncertainty it has created, have made it necessary for Atria’s management to critically assess the company’s assets, liabilities, income and expenses, even though the impacts of the pandemic on Atria’s operations have been moderate.
[p.068] The management has assessed the uncertainties and risks and exercised discretion when applying the accounting policies.
[p.068] The following paragraphs briefly describe the effect of the COVID-19 pandemic on the application of the company’s accounting policies.
[p.068] The actual accounting policies are presented later in the “Consolidated Accounting policies” section.
[p.068] Intangible and tangible assets and inventories: Atria’s operations have continued throughout the pandemic without interruption and sales have increased.
[p.068] There has been no need for additional depreciation and Atria’s policy regarding depreciation remains unchanged.
[p.068] Unusual impairment of goods in stock has not occurred.
[p.068] On the closing date of the reporting period, Atria also reviewed any indication of impairment of intangible assets.
[p.068] The interest rates used in the calculations have been checked.
[p.068] The Group has conducted impairment tests on goodwill and intangible assets with indefinite useful lives.
[p.068] NOTES TO THE CONSOLIDATED FINANCIAL STATEMENTS, IFRS 69
[p.069] Front page Atria in brief Atria’s key indicators CEO’s review Strategy 2021–2025 Strategy 2016–2020 Operating environment Business area reviews Atria Finland Atria Sweden Atria Denmark & Estonia Atria Russia Research and Development Financial Statements and Corporate Governance Financial Statements and Corporate Governance Auditor’s report Corporate Governance Statement Investor reporting Contact information Atria’s Annual Report 2020 NOTES TO THE CONSOLIDATED FINANCIAL STATEMENTS, IFRS The calculation to test the impairment of intangible assets is based on a series of figures from a five-year strategic period which is annually assessed, taking into account any changes in the business environment, measures taken by Atria and the results achieved.
[p.069] Each of Atria’s business areas has prepared its own five-year series, and the continuation of the COVID-19 pandemic in 2021 has been taken into account in the first year of the series.
[p.069] Together with the business areas, the Group’s Management Team has assessed how realistic the series is during and after the pandemic, as well as the risks.
[p.069] The figures were finally also reviewed by the Board, which approved the proposals made.
[p.069] No indications of impairment were detected.
[p.069] Impairment testing and sensitivity analyses are described in more detail in Note 15.
[p.069] Right-of-use assets and lease liabilities: The Group has leased properties, machinery and equipment.
[p.069] The lease contracts are made for a fixed period or are valid until further notice.
[p.069] The contract period for leases that are valid until further notice, as well as any options to extend them, are assessed on a case-by-case basis.
[p.069] COVID-19 has not affected the terms of Atria’s leases and Atria has not received any lease relief.
[p.069] Revenue recognition and management of liquidity risk: Atria’s total sales have developed favourably during the pandemic and there has been no need to change the revenue recognition policies.
[p.069] As a result of increased sales and good results, the company’s financial position and cash flow were good during the financial year and, despite the exceptional circumstances, Atria has managed to refinance its maturing commercial papers with new ones.
[p.069] Cash and cash equivalents increased by approximately EUR 30 million during the first quarter, but were reduced to levels closer to normal during the second and third quarters.
[p.069] Trade receivables: Atria’s trade receivables from consumer goods customers are short-term and do not include significant financial components.
[p.069] Consumer product customers are mainly central wholesale businesses.
[p.069] Some of the trade receivables are sold to finance companies.
[p.069] The sold trade receivables are derecognised on the balance sheet when the finance company has settled the payment for the receivables and when all material risks and benefits related to the ownership have transferred to the buyer.
[p.069] Each Group company has assessed their trade receivables and their age distribution.
[p.069] Atria has evaluated its model for expected credit losses from trade receivables, which takes into account macroeconomic developments.
[p.069] It was not necessary to make material changes to the amount of recognised credit loss provision.
[p.069] Employee benefits: Due to the COVID-19 pandemic, employers were given a discount of 2.6% on their TyEL contributions during the period from 1 May to 31 December 2020.
[p.069] In Sweden, the state reimbursed some of the salary costs and social security contributions for sick leaves caused by the coronavirus from 1 March to 31 December 2020.
[p.069] No grants or subsidies related to the COVID-19 pandemic were received in Atria’s other business areas.
[p.069] Acquired operations: During the review period, Atria Finland acquired the entire share capital of Domretor Oy.
[p.069] Because the assets and liabilities acquired in business combinations are measured at fair value at the time of acquisition, Atria’s management has assessed the value of the assets, compared them with market prices and made assumptions of their future use.
[p.069] The liabilities have also been critically assessed.
[p.069] The management believes that the assessments and assumptions are sufficiently detailed to be used as the basis for fair value measurement.
[p.069] Taxes: In connection with the financial statements, Atria’s management has assessed the effect of uncertainty over tax treatment in accordance with IFRIC 23.
[p.069] Atria has not taken advantage of the tax reliefs granted by the tax authorities in connection with the COVID-19 pandemic and income taxes are recognised on the basis of the taxable result for the year.
[p.069] Deferred tax assets have been written down in Russia, because the Company did not foresee convincing evidence of future opportunities to offset tax losses.
[p.069] As a result of COVID-19 subsidies, it is not possible to use a group subsidy in Sweden to equalise the taxable results of the companies.
[p.069] This will slightly increase the income taxes paid by our Swedish companies.
[p.069] CHANGES IN ACCOUNTING POLICIES AND DISCLOSURES a) New and amended standards, effective for financial periods beginning on or after 1 January 2020 Definition of ‘material’ – amendments to IAS 1 and IAS 8 The IASB has made amendments to IAS 1 Presentation of Financial Statements and IAS 8 Accounting Policies, Changes in Accounting Estimates and Errors which use a consistent definition of materiality throughout International Financial Reporting Standards and the Conceptual Framework for Financial Reporting, clarify when information is material and incorporate some of the guidance in IAS 1 about immaterial information.
[p.069] Atria takes into account the changed definition of materiality in its consolidated financial statements and for publication in the data.
[p.069] 70
[p.070] Front page Atria in brief Atria’s key indicators CEO’s review Strategy 2021–2025 Strategy 2016–2020 Operating environment Business area reviews Atria Finland Atria Sweden Atria Denmark & Estonia Atria Russia Research and Development Financial Statements and Corporate Governance Financial Statements and Corporate Governance Auditor’s report Corporate Governance Statement Investor reporting Contact information Atria’s Annual Report 2020 b) Significant new standards and interpretations that have been issued, but will not become effective until after 1 January 2020 Classification of liabilities into current or non-current items - Amendments to IAS 1 The narrow-scope amendments to IAS 1 Presentation of Financial Statements clarify that liabilities are classified as either current or non-current, depending on the rights that exist at the end of the reporting period.
[p.070] Classification is unaffected by the expectations of the entity or events after the reporting date.
[p.070] The amendments also clarify what IAS 1 means when it refers to the ‘settlement’ of a liability.
[p.070] The amendments could affect the classification of liabilities, particularly for entities that previously considered management’s intentions to determine classification and for some liabilities that can be converted into equity.
[p.070] They must be applied retrospectively in accordance with the normal requirements in IAS 8 Accounting Policies, Changes in Accounting Estimates and Errors.
[p.070] In May 2020, the IASB issued an Exposure Draft proposing to defer the effective date of the amendments to 1 January 2023.
[p.070] Atria is currently assessing the impact of these amedments.
[p.070] Accounting policies for the consolidated financial statements SUBSIDIARIES The consolidated financial statements include the parent company Atria Plc and all its subsidiaries.
[p.070] Subsidiaries are companies controlled by the Group.
[p.070] The Group controls an entity when the Group is exposed to or entitled to variable returns from its involvement with the entity, and can affect those returns through its power over the entity.
[p.070] Subsidiaries acquired during the financial year are consolidated from the date of their acquisition and divested subsidiaries are included up to their date of sale.
[p.070] Business combinations are treated using the acquisition method of accounting.
[p.070] Consideration transferred, and the identifiable acquired assets and assumed liabilities of the acquired business are measured at fair value at acquisition date.
[p.070] Consideration transferred includes the fair value of an asset or liability arising from a contingent consideration arrangement.
[p.070] The costs of acquisition are charged to the income statement during the period in which they are incurred and the related services are received.
[p.070] The net assets and accepted and contingent liabilities acquired in business combinations are measured at fair value at the time of the acquisition.
[p.070] The interest of non-controlling owners in the acquisition target is recognised on acquisition basis either at fair value or based on their relative share of the identifiable net assets of the acquisition target.
[p.070] Where the consideration transferred with the non-controlling interest and the fair value of the previously held interest exceed the fair value of the acquired net assets, the excess is recorded as goodwill on the balance sheet.
[p.070] If the sum of the consideration, the amount of the non-controlling interest and previously held interest is less than the fair value of the acquired net assets, the difference is recorded in the income statement.
[p.070] All intra-Group transactions, receivables and liabilities and income and expenses are eliminated.
[p.070] Profits and losses due to intra-Group transactions leading to the recognition of an asset are also eliminated.
[p.070] The accounting policies applied by subsidiaries have been revised to match the Group policies, where necessary.
[p.070] The parent company’s changes of ownership of the subsidiaries, which do not lead to a loss of control, are treated as equity transactions.
[p.070] When shares are purchased from non-controlling shareholders, the difference between the consideration paid and the balance sheet value of the share acquired of the net assets of the subsidiary is recognised in equity.
[p.070] Profit or loss from the sale of shares to non-controlling shareholders is also recognised in equity.
[p.070] When control or major influence by the Group ceases to exist, any remaining interest is measured at fair value on the date of the loss of control, and the change in balance sheet value is recognised in the income statement.
[p.070] This fair value serves as the original balance sheet value when the remaining interest is later recognised as an associated company, a joint venture or financial assets.
[p.070] In addition, the amounts of said entity previously recognised in other comprehensive income are treated as if the Group had directly disposed of the associated assets and liabilities.
[p.070] This may mean that amounts previously recognised as other comprehensive income are reclassified to the income statement.
[p.070] ASSOCIATED COMPANIES AND JOINT ARRANGEMENTS Associates are companies in which the Group holds between 20% and 50% of the voting rights, and in which the Group has significant influence, but which is does not control.
[p.070] A joint arrangement is an arrangement in which two or more parties have joint control.
[p.070] Investments in joint arrangements are classified as either joint operations or joint ventures, depending on the contractual rights and obligations of each investor.
[p.070] A joint operation is a joint arrangement whereby the parties that have joint control of the arrangement have rights to the assets and obligations for the liabilities related to the arrangement.
[p.070] A joint venture is a joint arrangement whereby the parties that have joint control of the arrangement have rights to the net assets of the arrangement.
[p.070] The Group’s joint arrangements are joint ventures.
[p.070] Investments in associates and joint ventures are consolidated using the equity method.
[p.070] When using the equity method, the investment is initially recognised at acquisition cost, and this amount is increased or decreased to recognise the investor’s share of the subsequent profits or losses of the investee after the time of acquisition.
[p.070] The Group’s investment in associates and joint ventures includes any goodwill identified on the acquisition.
[p.070] NOTES TO THE CONSOLIDATED FINANCIAL STATEMENTS, IFRS 71
[p.071] Front page Atria in brief Atria’s key indicators CEO’s review Strategy 2021–2025 Strategy 2016–2020 Operating environment Business area reviews Atria Finland Atria Sweden Atria Denmark & Estonia Atria Russia Research and Development Financial Statements and Corporate Governance Financial Statements and Corporate Governance Auditor’s report Corporate Governance Statement Investor reporting Contact information Atria’s Annual Report 2020 NOTES TO THE CONSOLIDATED FINANCIAL STATEMENTS, IFRS If the interest in an associate company is reduced, but significant influence is retained, only a proportionate share of the amounts previously recognised in other comprehensive income is reclassified as profit or loss.
[p.071] The Group’s share of associates’ post-acquisition profits or losses is recognised under operating profit on the income statement.
[p.071] The balance sheet value of the investment is adjusted accordingly.
[p.071] If the Group’s share of the loss of an associate is equal to or exceeds its interest in the associate, including any other unsecured receivables, the Group will not recognise further losses if it does not have a legal or factual obligation to do so, and it has not made payments on behalf of the associate.
[p.071] FOREIGN CURRENCY TRANSLATION Items included in the financial statements of each of the Group companies are measured using the currency of the primary economic environment in which the entity operates (‘the functional currency’).
[p.071] The consolidated financial statements are presented in euros (EUR), which is the parent company’s functional currency, and the parent company’s and the Group’s presentation currency.
[p.071] Foreign currency transactions are translated using the exchange rates prevailing on the date of the transaction.
[p.071] Foreign currency receivables and liabilities are translated using the exchange rate prevailing on the end of the reporting period.
[p.071] Exchange differences arising from translation are recognised in the income statement and presented in the operating profit.
[p.071] Exchange gains and losses from forward exchange agreements protecting financial transactions and foreign currency-denominated loans are included in financial income and expenses, excluding exchange rate changes of derivative financial instruments that are qualifying cash flow hedges.
[p.071] These exchange rate differences have been recognised in other comprehensive income.
[p.071] The income statements and balance sheet items of the Group companies outside the euro area are accounted for in the currency that is the currency of the operating region of the company in question.
[p.071] The income statements of Group companies outside the euro area are translated into euros at the average exchange rate for the reporting period and the balance sheets at the closing exchange rate.
[p.071] Differences resulting from the translation are recognised as part of translation differences in other comprehensive income.
[p.071] The translation differences arising from the elimination of the acquisition costs of subsidiaries outside the euro area and the hedge profits derived from the corresponding net investments are also recognised in other comprehensive income.
[p.071] When a foreign operation is partially disposed of or sold, exchange rate differences in equity are recognised in the income statement.
[p.071] Goodwill and fair value adjustments arising on the acquisition of the foreign entity are treated as assets and liabilities of the foreign entity and translated at the closing rate.
[p.071] The exchange differences arising from this are recognised in other comprehensive income.
[p.071] PROPERTY, PLANT AND EQUIPMENT Property, plant and equipment are recognised at the cost of purchase or construction less accumulated depreciation and impairment losses.
[p.071] If the tangible fixed asset consists of several parts with different useful lives, each part is treated as a separate asset.
[p.071] The costs arising from replacing the part are capitalised.
[p.071] Other subsequent expenditure is included in the acquisition cost only if it is probable that the future benefit connected to the asset will benefit the Group, and the acquisition cost of the asset can be reliably determined.
[p.071] All other repair and maintenance costs are recognised in the income statement as an expense as incurred.
[p.071] Depreciation is recorded using a straight-line method over the estimated useful lives of the assets as follows: • Buildings ..................................................25–50 years • Machinery and equipment ....................5–30 years • Other tangible assets ..............................
[p.071] 5–10 years No depreciation is carried out on land and water.
[p.071] Asset items that cannot be recognised under property, plant and equipment due to their nature or depreciation periods are recognised as other tangible assets.
[p.071] The residual value and useful lives of assets are reviewed annually at the closing of the accounts and, if necessary, adjusted so that the balance sheet value is equal to the recoverable amount.
[p.071] The depreciation of property, plant and equipment ends when the asset item is classified as available for sale in accordance with IFRS 5 Non-current Assets Held for Sale and Discontinued Operations.
[p.071] Gains and losses on the disposal or transfer of property, plant or equipment are included in other operating income or expenses.
[p.071] RIGHT-OF-USE ASSETS The Group has leased properties, machinery and equipment.
[p.071] The lease contracts are made for a fixed period or are valid until further notice.
[p.071] The contract period for leases valid until further notice is assessed on a case-by-case basis.
[p.071] The contracts may include options to extend the lease.
[p.071] A right-of-use asset and a corresponding liability is recognised for leases when the leased asset is available for use by the Group.
[p.071] Assets and liabilities arising from leases are initially measured at present value.
[p.071] 72
[p.072] Front page Atria in brief Atria’s key indicators CEO’s review Strategy 2021–2025 Strategy 2016–2020 Operating environment Business area reviews Atria Finland Atria Sweden Atria Denmark & Estonia Atria Russia Research and Development Financial Statements and Corporate Governance Financial Statements and Corporate Governance Auditor’s report Corporate Governance Statement Investor reporting Contact information Atria’s Annual Report 2020 Right-of-use assets are measured at acquisition cost, which includes the following items: • The original amount of the lease liability (see ‘Lease liabilities’ for more information) • Lease payments made before the beginning of the contract less any incentives received • Initial direct costs • Restoration costs.
[p.072] Lease payments are discounted using the interest rate implicit in the lease.
[p.072] If this interest rate is unknown, the lessee’s incremental borrowing rate will be used.
[p.072] This is the rate that the lessee would have to pay to borrow the necessary funds over a similar term and with a similar security.
[p.072] Depreciation for right-of-use assets is usually recognised on a straight-line basis over the useful life of the asset, or the lease period if shorter.
[p.072] If it is reasonably certain that the Group will exercise the purchase option, the useful life will be used as the depreciation period for the asset.
[p.072] The company assesses the impairment of right-of-use assets in accordance with IAS 36 Impairment of Assets.
[p.072] Payments related to short-term leases and leases of low-value assets are recognised as expenses on a straight-line basis.
[p.072] Leases with a term of 12 months or less are considered to be short-term leases.
[p.072] Atria does not apply the IFRS 16 standard to intangible assets in accordance with IAS 38.
[p.072] INTANGIBLE ASSETS Goodwill: Goodwill represents the Group’s share of the difference between the consideration transferred and the identifiable acquired assets and assumed liabilities measured at fair value on the acquisition date.
[p.072] Goodwill is tested annually for impairment.
[p.072] For this purpose, goodwill has been allocated to cash-generating units.
[p.072] The Group’s cash-generating units are classified based on subsidiaries’ operations and location.
[p.072] These are Atria Finland, Atria Sweden, Atria Denmark, Atria Estonia and Atria Russia.
[p.072] Goodwill is recognised on the balance sheet at cost less impairment losses.
[p.072] An impairment loss recognised for goodwill is not reversed.
[p.072] Other intangible assets: An Intangible asset is initially capitalised on the balance sheet at cost if the cost can be measured reliably and it is probable that the company will receive future economic benefit from the asset.
[p.072] Intangible assets with a limited useful life are amortised on a straight-line basis over their estimated useful lives.
[p.072] Intangible assets with indefinite useful lives are not amortised but are tested annually for impairment.
[p.072] The depreciation periods are as follows: • Customer and supplier relationships ...........
[p.072] 3–8 years • Trademarks .......................................................5–20 years • Other intangible assets*) ................................
[p.072] 5–10 years *) Includes software and subscription fees, among other items IMPAIRMENT OF NON-CURRENT ASSETS On each balance sheet date, the Group reviews non-current assets for any indications of impairment.
[p.072] If there are such indications, the amount recoverable from the asset is estimated.
[p.072] The amount of cash recoverable from goodwill and intangible assets with indefinite useful lives is assessed annually and whenever there are indications of impairment.
[p.072] The recoverable amount is the higher of the present value of the future cash flows (value in use) and the fair value of the asset less costs of disposal.
[p.072] If the recoverable amount cannot be assessed per item, the impairment need is observed on the level of cash-flow generating units – that is, at the lowest unit level that is mainly independent of other units and at which cash flows can be distinguished from other cash flows.
[p.072] Impairment loss is recognised if the balance sheet value of the asset is higher than the recoverable amount.
[p.072] Impairment loss is recognised immediately in the income statement.
[p.072] If the impairment loss concerns a cash-generating unit, it is first allocated to reduce the goodwill and then to reduce the other assets of the unit pro rata.
[p.072] The useful life of the depreciated asset is re-evaluated in connection with the recognition of an impairment loss.
[p.072] An impairment loss recognised for an asset other than goodwill is reversed if there has been a change in the estimates used to determine the amount recoverable from the asset.
[p.072] However, the impairment loss may not be reversed in excess of what the asset’s balance sheet value would be without the recognition of the impairment loss.
[p.072] An impairment loss recognised for goodwill is never reversed.
[p.072] INVENTORIES Inventories are measured at cost or probable net realisable value, whichever is lower.
[p.072] The acquisition cost is determined using the average price method.
[p.072] The acquisition cost for finished and unfinished products consists of raw materials, direct labour costs, other direct costs, and the appropriate share of manufacturing-related variable overheads and fixed overheads at a normal level of operations.
[p.072] The net realisable value is the estimated selling price in the ordinary course of business, less the estimated selling expenses.
[p.072] BIOLOGICAL ASSETS The Group’s biological assets are living animals.
[p.072] They are measured at fair value less estimated sales-related expenses.
[p.072] Productive animals are included in tangible assets and other animals are included in inventories.
[p.072] NOTES TO THE CONSOLIDATED FINANCIAL STATEMENTS, IFRS 73
[p.073] Front page Atria in brief Atria’s key indicators CEO’s review Strategy 2021–2025 Strategy 2016–2020 Operating environment Business area reviews Atria Finland Atria Sweden Atria Denmark & Estonia Atria Russia Research and Development Financial Statements and Corporate Governance Financial Statements and Corporate Governance Auditor’s report Corporate Governance Statement Investor reporting Contact information Atria’s Annual Report 2020 NOTES TO THE CONSOLIDATED FINANCIAL STATEMENTS, IFRS The fair value of productive animals has been measured at cost less an expense corresponding to a reduction of value in use caused by ageing.
[p.073] There is no available market price for productive animals.
[p.073] The fair value of slaughter animals is equal to their market price, which is based on the company’s slaughter animal procurement/sales.
[p.073] FINANCIAL ASSETS Classification In accordance with IFRS 9 Financial Instruments, the Group’s financial assets are classified in the following categories: financial assets at amortised cost, financial assets at fair value through other comprehensive income and financial assets at fair value through profit or loss.
[p.073] The classification is based on business models used for the management of the financial assets and on the contractual cash flows of the financial assets.
[p.073] The purchases and sales of financial assets are recognised on the transaction date.
[p.073] Financial assets are classified as non-current assets when they fall due more than 12 months from the closing date.
[p.073] If the financial assets are intended to be kept for less than 12 months, they are classified as current assets.
[p.073] The Group derecognises financial assets when it has lost its right to receive the cash flows, or when it has substantially transferred the risks and rewards of ownership to an external party.
[p.073] Financial assets recognised at amortised cost: Trade receivables, loan receivables and other receivables recognised at amortised cost are recognised less expected impairment loss.
[p.073] Trade receivables recognised at fair value in other comprehensive income are recognised at fair value.
[p.073] Changes in fair value are recognised in other comprehensive income, excluding impairment losses, which are recognised through profit or loss.
[p.073] Non-current trade receivables and interest-bearing loan receivables are primarily payment time provided to secure the supply of meat raw material and loans to primary production customers.
[p.073] These items are subject to the general impairment model.
[p.073] If there is no significant increase in credit risk, the estimated amount of credit losses is based on the expected credit losses of 12 months and, in other cases, on credit losses expected for the entire lifetime.
[p.073] Atria’s trade receivables from consumer goods customers are short-term and do not include significant financial components.
[p.073] These trade receivables are subject to a simplified method in which the estimated amount of credit losses is based on the expected credit losses over the receivables’ lifetime.
[p.073] Some trade receivables in the Group are sold to finance companies.
[p.073] The sold trade receivables are derecognised on the balance sheet when the finance company has settled the payment for the receivables and when all material risks and benefits related to the ownership have transferred to the buyer.
[p.073] Trade receivables that may be sold are classified as financial assets recognised at fair value in other comprehensive income.
[p.073] Equity investments recognised at fair value through other comprehensive income: The ‘other financial assets’ account includes equity investments in other companies (both listed and unlisted shares).
[p.073] The shares are not held for trading.
[p.073] In connection with the original recognition, the Group has made an irreversible selection of their inclusion in this group.
[p.073] Listed shares are recognised at fair value, which is based on their stock market price.
[p.073] Unlisted shares are recognised though valuation methods, or at acquisition price if it essentially corresponds to the fair value.
[p.073] When the shares are disposed of, the balance included in other comprehensive income is reclassified in retained earnings and will not be recognised through profit or loss.
[p.073] At fair value through profit or loss: Derivatives not subject to hedge accounting are recognised at fair value through profit or loss.
[p.073] Derivatives are initially recognised on the balance sheet at acquisition price, which is equal to their fair value, and later at the fair value of the end date of the review period.
[p.073] Both unrealised and realised profit or loss attributable to changes in the fair value are recognised through profit or loss during the period in which they occur.
[p.073] Cash and cash equivalents consist of cash, bank deposits withdrawable on demand and other cash.
[p.073] Credit facilities related to Group accounts are included in non-current financial liabilities.
[p.073] FINANCIAL LIABILITIES The Group’s loans are classified either in financial liabilities recognised at amortised cost or in financial liabilities recognised at fair value through profit or loss.
[p.073] Financial liabilities are classified as current unless the Group has an absolute right to postpone the payment of the debt to a date at least 12 months from the end date of the review period.
[p.073] Financial liabilities (or parts thereof) are derecognised on the balance sheet only when the debt no longer exists – that is, when the obligation specified in the contract has been fulfilled or revoked, or has expired.
[p.073] Financial liabilities recognised at amortised cost: Loans taken out by the Group are included in financial liabilities recognised at amortised cost.
[p.073] They are initially recognised at fair value, using the effective interest rate method.
[p.073] Following the initial recognition, loans are recognised at amortised cost.
[p.073] Interest on loans is amortised over the loan’s maturity period through profit or loss, using the effective interest rate method.
[p.073] Financial liabilities recognised at fair value through profit or loss: Financial liabilities recognised at fair value through profit or loss include derivatives that do not meet the criteria for hedge accounting.
[p.073] Both unrealised and realised profit or loss attributable to changes in the fair value of derivatives are recognised through profit or loss during the period in which they occur.
[p.073] 74
[p.074] Front page Atria in brief Atria’s key indicators CEO’s review Strategy 2021–2025 Strategy 2016–2020 Operating environment Business area reviews Atria Finland Atria Sweden Atria Denmark & Estonia Atria Russia Research and Development Financial Statements and Corporate Governance Financial Statements and Corporate Governance Auditor’s report Corporate Governance Statement Investor reporting Contact information Atria’s Annual Report 2020 LEASE LIABILITIES The Group has leased properties, machinery and equipment.
[p.074] When a contract is established, the Group determines whether the contract is a lease contract or includes a lease contract.
[p.074] A lease is a contract or part of a contract that conveys the right to use the underlying asset for a period of time in exchange for consideration.
[p.074] Lease contracts are made for a fixed period or are valid until further notice.
[p.074] The contract period for leases valid until further notice is assessed on a case-by-case basis.
[p.074] The contracts may include options to extend the lease.
[p.074] A right-of-use asset and a corresponding liability is recognised for leases when the leased asset is available for use by the Group.
[p.074] Liabilities arising from leases are initially measured at present value.
[p.074] Lease liabilities include the net fair value of the following lease payments: • Fixed payments • Variable payments that are based on an index or price level and that are initially measured using the index or price on the contract date • Amounts that the Group is expected to pay based on residual value guarantees • The execution price of a purchase option if it is reasonably certain that the Group will exercise the option • Payments arising from the premature termination of a lease if the exercise of this option has been taken into account in the lease period • Lease payments based on options to extend a lease if it is reasonably certain these options will be exercised.
[p.074] Lease payments are discounted using the interest rate implicit in the lease.
[p.074] If this interest rate is not known, the lessee’s incremental borrowing rate will be used.
[p.074] This is the rate of interest that the lessee would have to pay to borrow the funds necessary for an asset of a similar value to the right-of-use asset over a similar term and with a similar security in a similar economic environment.
[p.074] To determine the incremental borrowing rate, the Group uses, as far as possible, financing that it has recently been provided by an external party, adjusted for changes in financial circumstances that have occurred since the financing was granted.
[p.074] The Group is exposed to possible increases in lease payments based on an index or price level.
[p.074] These are not taken into account in lease liabilities until their materialisation.
[p.074] When changes in lease payments based on an index or price level are materialised, lease liabilities are reviewed and are adjusted against the right-of-use asset.
[p.074] Lease payments to be made are allocated to equity and financial expenses.
[p.074] Financial expenses are recognised through profit or loss over the lease period so that the interest rate for the remaining liabilities remains the same for each reporting period.
[p.074] Payments related to short-term leases and leases of low-value assets are recognised as expenses on a straight-line basis.
[p.074] Leases with a term of 12 months or less are considered to be short-term leases.
[p.074] Atria does not apply the IFRS 16 standard to leases of intangible assets in accordance with IAS 38.
[p.074] HEDGE ACCOUNTING Derivative contracts are initially recognised at fair value on the contract date and are subsequently remeasured at fair value at the end of each reporting period.
[p.074] The recognition of changes in the fair value of derivatives depends on whether the derivative instrument qualifies for hedge accounting and if so, on the hedged item.
[p.074] Derivatives not subject to hedge accounting are defined as hedges of interest rate, currency or electricity price risks associated with a recognised asset or liability, or a highly probable forecast transaction (cash flow hedge).
[p.074] When a derivative is subject to hedge accounting, the Group documents the relationship between each hedging instrument and the hedged asset, as well as the risk management objective and the strategy applied to it, at the beginning of the hedging arrangement.
[p.074] Through this process, the hedging instrument is connected to the assets and liabilities or the forecast transactions related to the instrument.
[p.074] Risk management objectives and strategies for undertaking various hedge transactions are also documented.
[p.074] The Group documents its assessment, both at hedge inception and on an ongoing basis, of whether the derivatives that are used in hedge transactions are highly effective in offsetting changes in fair values or cash flows of hedged items.
[p.074] The full fair value of a hedging derivative is classified as a non-current asset or liability when the maturity of the hedged item is more than 12 months and as a current asset or liability when the remaining maturity of the hedged item is 12 months or less.
[p.074] Derivatives held for trading are classified as current assets or liabilities.
[p.074] Valuation principles: The fair value of forward exchange agreements is calculated by applying the forward rate on the balance sheet date.
[p.074] The fair value of interest rate swaps is calculated by discounting the future cash flows using interest rate curves for the currencies in question.
[p.074] Electricity derivatives are measured at fair value using the market prices at the balance sheet date.
[p.074] Cash flow hedge: The effective portion of changes in the fair value of derivatives that are designated and qualify as cash flow hedges is recognised in other comprehensive income and accumulated in equity.
[p.074] The gain or loss related to the ineffective portion is recognised immediately in the income statement under the appropriate item.
[p.074] Gains and losses accumulated in equity are reclassified in the income statement in the periods when the hedged item affects profit or loss (for example, when the forecast purchase that is hedged takes place).
[p.074] However, when the forecast transaction that is hedged results in the recognition of a non-financial asset (for NOTES TO THE CONSOLIDATED FINANCIAL STATEMENTS, IFRS 75
[p.075] Front page Atria in brief Atria’s key indicators CEO’s review Strategy 2021–2025 Strategy 2016–2020 Operating environment Business area reviews Atria Finland Atria Sweden Atria Denmark & Estonia Atria Russia Research and Development Financial Statements and Corporate Governance Financial Statements and Corporate Governance Auditor’s report Corporate Governance Statement Investor reporting Contact information Atria’s Annual Report 2020 NOTES TO THE CONSOLIDATED FINANCIAL STATEMENTS, IFRS example, inventories or fixed assets), the gains and losses previously deferred in equity are transferred from equity and included in the initial acquisition cost of the asset.
[p.075] The deferred amounts are ultimately recognised in costs of goods sold in the case of inventories, or in depreciation in the case of fixed assets.
[p.075] When a hedging instrument expires or is sold, or when a hedge no longer meets the criteria for hedge accounting, any cumulative gain or loss existing in equity at the time remains in equity and is recognised in the income statement only when the forecast transaction occurs.
[p.075] When a forecast transaction is no longer expected to occur, the cumulative gain or loss that was reported in equity is immediately transferred to the income statement under the appropriate item.
[p.075] ASSETS CLASSIFIED AS HELD FOR SALE Non-current assets are classified as held for sale if their balance sheet value is to be recovered through a sale transaction rather than through continuing use.
[p.075] This condition is regarded as having been met only when the sale is highly probable, and the asset is available for immediate sale in its present condition and is subject only to terms that are usual and customary.
[p.075] Furthermore, management must be committed to the sale, which should be expected to occur within one year of the date of classification.
[p.075] Immediately before being classified as held for sale, these assets are measured in accordance with the applicable IFRS standards.
[p.075] Thereafter, the assets are measured at the lower of their balance sheet value and fair value less cost to sell.
[p.075] These assets are no longer depreciated after the classification.
[p.075] EQUITY Ordinary shares are presented as share capital.
[p.075] Expenses related to the issue or acquisition of equity instruments are presented as a deductible item under equity.
[p.075] If a Group company acquires shares in the company, the consideration paid for them and the expenses arising directly from the acquisition, taking into consideration the tax effect, are deducted from the shareholders’ equity until the shares are either cancelled or reissued.
[p.075] If the shares are reissued, the consideration received for them less transaction costs directly attributable to the shares is included in the shareholders’ equity, taking into consideration the tax effect.
[p.075] PROVISIONS A provision is entered when the Group has a legal or constructive obligation as a result of a past event, and it is probable that an outflow of resources will be required to settle the obligation and the amount of the obligation can be reliably estimated.
[p.075] Provisions are measured at the present value of the expenses required to cover the obligation.
[p.075] The amounts of provisions are reviewed on each balance sheet date and adjusted to correspond to the best estimate at that time.
[p.075] Changes in provisions are recognised in the income statement in the same item in which the original provision was entered.
[p.075] REVENUE RECOGNITION Atria sells food products, animal feed, traded animals and services.
[p.075] Sales revenue is recognised based on customer contracts.
[p.075] The contracts specify the contractual obligations and the prices applicable to them.
[p.075] Atria does not have consolidated contractual obligations or obligations to be met over time, advance payments or warranty obligations.
[p.075] Atria recognises both the revenue and the receivable when control over the goods or service is transferred to the customer.
[p.075] Delivery usually takes place in Finland within 24 hours, and control and risks are transferred in connection with delivery.
[p.075] In export deals, the company estimates the time when control transfers to the customer specific to each delivery in accordance with the terms and time of delivery.
[p.075] Sales prices are not adjusted for the time value of money, because the period between the handover of the products and the payment made by the customer is less than a year.
[p.075] Atria always allocates discounts, as well as any refunds following the sale, to the month of delivery, taking the customers’ full-year volume into account.
[p.075] In the recognition of sales revenue, Atria has identified two customer groups: consumer goods customers and primary production customers.
[p.075] Atria presents sales divided into these two revenue streams as part of the segment information in Note 1 and the division of receivables in Note 20.
[p.075] Atria considers these two customer groups to be the most material in terms of understanding the nature of sales revenue and cash flow arising from customer contracts.
[p.075] Most contracts with customers concern the sale of consumer products.
[p.075] Consumer goods customers are primarily central wholesale businesses.
[p.075] In addition, Atria sells traded animals and animal feed to primary production customers.
[p.075] EMPLOYEE BENEFITS Pension obligations: The Group companies have various local pension arrangements in their countries of operation.
[p.075] Pension arrangements are classified as either defined contribution plans or defined benefit pension plans.
[p.075] In defined contribution plans, the Group makes fixed payments into a separate unit.
[p.075] The Group has no legal or constructive obligation to make additional payments if the recipient of the payments cannot pay the pension benefits in question.
[p.075] All plans that do not fulfil these conditions are defined benefit pension plans.
[p.075] Payments made into defined contribution plans are recognised in the income statement in the reporting period to which they apply.
[p.075] The Group’s pension plans are mainly defined contribution plans.
[p.075] In defined benefit plans the company still has an ongoing obligation for the plan even after the payment for the period has been made.
[p.075] For arrangements classified 76
[p.076] Front page Atria in brief Atria’s key indicators CEO’s review Strategy 2021–2025 Strategy 2016–2020 Operating environment Business area reviews Atria Finland Atria Sweden Atria Denmark & Estonia Atria Russia Research and Development Financial Statements and Corporate Governance Financial Statements and Corporate Governance Auditor’s report Corporate Governance Statement Investor reporting Contact information Atria’s Annual Report 2020 as defined benefit plans, actuarial estimates acquired on a yearly basis serve as the grounds for recognising an expense and liability or asset in the financial statements.
[p.076] Actuarial gains or losses are recognised as equity refunds or a charge in other comprehensive income in the financial period in which they occur.
[p.076] Share-based payments: The Group has an incentive programme for the management where the payments are made in part as company shares and in part as cash.
[p.076] The remuneration awarded under the programme is measured at fair value at the time of awarding, and recognised in the income statement as an expense arising from employee benefits spread over the earning and engagement period.
[p.076] The amount of money paid in the arrangement is remeasured using the review period’s closing share price and recognised in the income statement as an expense from employee benefits spread over from the day of awarding until the money is transferred to the recipient.
[p.076] The final amount of the expense depends on the extent to which the conditions of the incentive programme are met.
[p.076] RESEARCH AND DEVELOPMENT EXPENSES Research expenditure is recognised as an expense in the income statement.
[p.076] Expenditure related to individual projects is capitalised on the balance sheet when there is enough certainty that the product in question is technically viable and that the product is likely to generate future economic benefits.
[p.076] Capitalised development expenditure is recognised in project-specific expenses over the useful life of the product.
[p.076] The asset is amortised from the time it is ready for use.
[p.076] The Group has no capitalised development expenses.
[p.076] GOVERNMENT GRANTS Grants received as compensation for expenses are recognised in the income statement, while expenses connected with the grant are entered as costs.
[p.076] Such grants are recognised under other operating income.
[p.076] The nature of the grants varies between countries, and the grants are only recognised after all the terms and conditions of the grant have been met, so the company does not have a repayment obligation arising from grants received.
[p.076] Government grants – such as grants received for the acquisition of property, plant and equipment – are recognised as a deduction in the balance sheet value of property, plant and equipment when it is reasonably certain that the grant will be received and that the Group company fulfils the prerequisites for receiving the grant.
[p.076] Grants are recognised as income in the form of lower depreciation during the useful life of the asset.
[p.076] INCOME TAXES The consolidated income statement includes the current taxes of Group companies based on taxable profit for the financial period in line with local tax regulations, as well as adjustments to previous years’ taxes and changes in deferred taxes.
[p.076] Taxes are entered in the income statement unless they are related to other comprehensive income or items recognised directly in equity.
[p.076] In such cases, the tax is also entered in other comprehensive income or directly in equity.
[p.076] Taxes based on taxable profit for the financial year are calculated using the current tax rate in each country.
[p.076] Deferred taxes are recognised for all temporary differences between the balance sheet value and the tax base.
[p.076] The largest temporary differences arise from the depreciation of property, plants and equipment, and fair value measurements in connection with acquisitions.
[p.076] No deferred tax is recognised for non-deductible goodwill impairment, and no deferred tax is recognised for the undistributed profits of subsidiaries if the difference is unlikely to dissolve in the foreseeable future.
[p.076] Deferred tax is calculated using the tax rates provided on the balance sheet date.
[p.076] Deferred tax assets are recognised to the amount for which it is likely that taxable profit will be generated in the future against which the temporary difference can be utilised.
[p.076] Deferred tax assets are recognised for confirmed losses made by Group companies to the extent in which it is likely that the assets can be utilised to offset future taxable profits.
[p.076] NOTES TO THE CONSOLIDATED FINANCIAL STATEMENTS, IFRS 77

[p.077] SEGMENT INFORMATION, EUR 1,000 The Group’s operating segments are based on the Group’s internal organisational structure and internal financial reporting, which Atria’s Board of Directors uses in strategic and operative decision-making.
[p.077] The Board of Directors assesses the performance of the operating segments based on net sales, EBIT and return on capital employed for the year.
[p.077] The Group has four recognisable geographical segments that differ essentially from one another in terms of the functioning of the markets.
[p.077] Atria Finland, Atria Sweden, Atria Denmark & Estonia and Atria Russia.
[p.077] In addition, Group costs are now reported separately in unallocated items.
[p.077] Group costs consist of personnel and administration costs as well as other costs that are not allocated to the business areas.
[p.077] A segment’s assets and liabilities are items that can be directly attributed or reasonably allocated to the segment.
[p.077] Transactions between the segments take place at market prices.
[p.077] The Group has two major customers, and the value of the trade with each of them constitutes between 10% and 15% of the Group’s net sales.
[p.077] The net sales in question are reported in the operating segments Finland, Denmark & Estonia and Russia.
